As for the method of handling the new changes, Qian Tong (Zi Mengcai), who once held an important position in Xinjiang Province, is extremely familiar with the situation in Xinjiang. Qian is currently staying in Peiping and cabled the central government a few days ago, offering his opinions on how to handle the turmoil in Xinjiang. The content is roughly as follows: The Muslim rebellion in Xinjiang has lasted for two years. The cause of this is that Jin De'an indulged his fellow villagers in Hezhou and confiscated the land of the Hami Muslims, and placed the Mongolian princes under house arrest in the province, not allowing them to return to their banners, and even killing them, which incited a great chaos that was difficult to clean up. The central government is currently out of reach and unable to respond, but we must think of a way to remedy the situation. It is easy to talk about securing the area but those sent must be soldiers. How can they achieve their goals in a few months? It is suggested that the Executive Yuan first cable Ma Shaowu, the head of Kashi Gar administrative office (Shie Ying), to find a way to appease the situation. If the southern route is stable, the new situation will be easier to maintain. On the other hand, we should start using Han people who have registered in Xinjiang, such as Li Rong, the president of Dihua Administration Court, and Li Zhonglin, the former head of Tacheng. Zhonglin is proficient in Russian, Mongolian, Kazakh and other languages, and is a useful talent in the northwest. Jin De'an was suspicious and did not use them. The central government should recruit them quickly. On the other hand, a special envoy should be sent to Xinjiang in the shortest possible time to implement military and civilian separation. The overall situation in the northwest can then be saved.

Shanghai Municipal Farmers' Association Inauguration 100

The Shanghai Municipal Farmers' Association, in preparation since November of the 20th year, has been delayed until now due to various factors. It was finally approved by the Municipal Party Headquarters to hold its inaugural meeting yesterday morning at 9:00 AM on the third floor of the Municipal Party Headquarters. The Municipal Party Headquarters sent Zhou Lianze to attend and provide guidance, and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau sent Wu Huanru to attend and provide guidance. Guests included Huang Zhizhi (Municipal Assembly), Sun Daosheng (Journalists' Association), Wu Shuxing (Social Affairs Bureau), and over a hundred people, including all preparatory committee members and representatives from various districts. After the ceremony, discussions on proposals began, and the association's charter was approved. Officers and councilors were elected, and the meeting adjourned at 1:00 PM. The details are recorded below:

Meeting Order (1) Ring bell to begin the meeting, (2) Elect the chairman of the presidium, (3) All stand at attention, (4) Sing the Party song, (5) Pay the highest respects to the national flag, Party flag, and portrait of the late Premier, (6) The Chairman respectfully reads the late Premier's will, (7) Silent mourning, (8) Chairman's report, (9) Representative of the preparatory committee reports on the preparations, (10) Representatives of Party and government organs provide guidance, (11) Speeches by guests, (12) Approval of the charter, (13) Discussion of proposals, (14) Provisional motions, (15) Elections, (16) Shout slogans, (17) Photograph, (18) Adjournment.

District Representatives Aside from Zhabei District, they are: Pengpu District: Hou Shizhang, Wang Tongfu, Hou Junren; Yinhang District: Zhu Wenxiang, Sun Huazhong; Hunan District: Shen Ruoxu, Zhang Huijun; Fahua District: Liu Rong, Gu Siqing; Jiangwan District: Liu Daokui, Wu Ziju; Yangsi District: Hu Zhusan, Ma Jinpo; Yinxiang District: Lu Jingtan, Yang Xinshi; Gaohang District: Yu Zhenhui, Zhu Runsheng; Caohjing District: Wu Rugui, Zong Xiaojie.

Chairman's Report The presidium of the association was recommended by the preparatory committee to be chaired by Yu Zhenhui and Liu Daokui. Zhang Sheng was also added as chairman by the general meeting. Yu Zhenhui first reported, roughly saying that although this city is a prosperous metropolis, agricultural land still accounts for the largest proportion of the city's land, and farmers still account for the largest proportion of the city's population. While industry, commerce, and education all have organizations, farmers' organizations should be formed as soon as possible. This association could have been established earlier since preparations began two years ago, but it was interrupted by the January 28th Incident. Now, farmers' associations in various districts and representatives from various districts have been gradually elected, and today the inaugural meeting is officially held. In the future, we must make extra efforts to seek the welfare of all farmers in the city.

Preparatory Committee Report The preparatory committee recommended Zhang Huice to report, roughly saying that the Shanghai Municipal Farmers' Association has been in preparation for a year and a half, and it is only now that it has been announced that it has been established. Its responsibility to the preparatory committee can be said to have been fulfilled. However, the reasons why it could not be established earlier should be explained. After the association recommended Yu Zhenhui, Liu Daokui, and 13 others as preparatory committee members in November of the 20th year, it immediately began preparatory work. Before long, the January 28th Incident occurred, and the association's preparatory work was interrupted. Since the armistice, work could have been continued intermittently, but in April of that year, the central government issued a nationwide order that people's organizations that had not yet been organized should postpone their establishment. Therefore, the association also stagnated invisibly. It was not until November of the same year that it began to actively proceed. Currently, only one district, Zhabei, has not elected representatives to attend. The preparatory committee has presented it to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau, and they have chosen today to hold the inaugural meeting. As for economic and other reports, please refer to the association's inaugural special issue.

Speeches by Representatives Zhou Lianze, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, gave a speech, roughly saying that the Party attaches great importance to the farmers' movement. This can be confirmed in the farmers' movement proposal of the Second National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang. Farmers account for more than 85% of the national population, and agricultural products account for more than 90% of the national output. From these statistics, we can clearly understand the importance of the position of farmers in China. The late Premier once said, "If the farmers' movement is done well, then the national revolution will achieve a great success." However, looking at the tragic state of bankruptcy of the rural economy in China today, we cannot but attach importance to the farmers' movement. The reasons for the bankruptcy of the rural economy can be observed from both internal and external aspects. External reasons include the economic and political aggression of imperialism. Internal reasons include exorbitant taxes, and the exploitation of farmers by landlords, vagrants, local tyrants, and corrupt gentry, so that farmers cannot live in peace in the countryside and have to leave the countryside and go to the city. Therefore, if we want to seek the welfare of farmers, we must overthrow these two internal and external reactionary forces. After the representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters finished his speech, Wu Hengru, chief of the Second Section of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, gave a speech, roughly saying that the bankruptcy of China's rural economy today is undeniable. There are many reasons for its bankruptcy, but the most important reason is the low price of agricultural products. Taking China's main agricultural products, such as rice and cotton, as an example, the price of rice is now less than 10 yuan per dan, and the price of cotton is only about 12 yuan per dan. Due to the low price of agricultural products, farmers' income can hardly maintain their lives. Therefore, farmers have to leave the countryside and go to the city to make a living. Therefore, from the standpoint of farmers, we still hope that the price of agricultural products will rise. This view will be opposed by industry and commerce, whose reason is that if the price of domestic agricultural products rises, the market will be rejected by cheap imported goods. However, we observe that the methods used in rural China today are still very old. Therefore, we should apply scientific methods, which can increase production while reducing production costs. This is also a way to remedy the rural economy. Therefore, what I hope for in the future Municipal Farmers' Association is not to add the name of a municipal farmers' association to a certain telegram, but to use a scientific spirit to strive to improve production methods in order to seek the actual happiness of farmers. In addition, there were speeches by Sun Daosheng, representative of the Journalists' Association, and others, which were mostly encouraging and are omitted here.

Approval of Proposals After the representatives finished their speeches, they began to discuss the plan to improve the countryside: A. Regarding farmers' production: (1) According to the original types of agricultural products in the city and the needs of the citizens, collect good seeds for the preparation of seed exchange and distribution; (2) Request the municipal government to allocate funds to open a farmers' education center to display various new agricultural machines, improved seeds, and scientific fertilizers to guide farmers to experiment with their application. B. Regarding farmers' education: (1) Send a letter to the Municipal Education Bureau to set up a rural primary school in each of the 40 autonomous regions divided in the city; (2) Each district farmers' association should set up a farmers' night school, one or two, within its possible scope; (3) Send a letter to the Municipal Education Bureau to restore the public tea garden; (4) Publish regular periodicals. C. Regarding farmers' organizations: (1) Promote local autonomy; (2) Abolish the "Tu-Dong Bao-Jia" system; (3) Submit a request to amend the Farmers' Association: 1. The Municipal Farmers' Association directly under the Executive Yuan should be at the same level as the Provincial Farmers' Association; 2. Organize Farmers' Associations below the district level; (4) Subsidize the administrative expenses of Farmers' Associations in various districts. D. Regarding farmers' cooperation: (1) Request the municipal government to establish a farmers' bank; (2) Request the municipal government to allocate funds to establish an agricultural cooperation experimental farm; (3) Encourage farmers to try agricultural cooperation. E. Regarding rural construction: (4) Urge the government to implement the following matters in order to realize rural cities: 1. Widen the ridges in the fields; 2. Dredge the rivers in the city's agricultural areas; 3. Connect electric lights, running water, and telephones; 4. Add transportation tools (such as public buses, trucks, trams, etc.); 5. Establish public entertainment venues, parks, libraries, and other cultural institutions; 6. Raise funds to build hospitals, homes for the disabled, orphanages, and nursing homes, and other charitable facilities. F. Regarding farmers' morality: (1) Correct farmers' superstitious behaviors (welcoming gods, temple fairs, burning incense and praying, etc.); (2) Correct farmers' extravagant habits, such as lavish funerals and weddings, etc.; (3) Correct farmers' decadent customs, such as gambling and singing flower drum operas, etc.; (4) How to promote local autonomy; (5) Telegram to comfort the anti-Japanese soldiers; (6) Telegram to Comrade Hu Hanmin to enter Beijing to jointly face the national crisis; (7) Submit a request to the higher authorities to amend the Farmers' Association Law; (8) Raise funds for the "Shanghai Farmer" aircraft; (9) Submit a request to the municipal government to expand the city's temple property to expand the rural compulsory education fund.

Elected Officials The election results are: Officers: Lu Jingtan, Zhang Sheng, Liu Daokui, Liu Rong, Shen Ruoxu; Councilors: Wu Hengru, Zhou Funong, Lin Wuyan, Wang Shuji, Wu Ziju, Wang Tongfu, Feng Xiancheng, Zong Xiaojie, Pan Hongding, Xu Baoming, Ling Zhibin, Zhu Wenxiang, Wu Rugui, Hou Junren, Gu Junqing, Yang Xinshi, Ma Jinpo, Hou Shichang, Hu Zhusan.

Declaration The main points of the declaration are: (1) Develop rural education to instill farmers' knowledge; (2) Promote local autonomy to improve rural organizations; (3) Promote agricultural cooperation to improve farmers' lives; (omitted) In summary, the above four points are the essential methods to relieve farmers and revitalize the countryside today. This association will do its best and be determined to proceed to the end. It is hoped that all farmers in the city will work together under the leadership of this association, and that people from all walks of life will cooperate and assist. This is deeply appreciated.

General Meeting Telegram The association issued a telegram in the name of the general meeting: (1) To comfort the anti-Japanese soldiers, etc.: To all the newspapers across the country, forward to the front-line soldiers for your review. You are resisting with blood and repeatedly defeating strong enemies, fighting for the status of our nation, fighting for the national character of our country, and fighting for the justice of the world's powers. Your sacrifice is just and your righteousness is as thin as the sky. On behalf of all the farmers in the city, the enemy association first expresses its condolences. (2) Please Comrade Hu Hanmin to enter Beijing to jointly face the national crisis, etc.: To all the newspapers across the country, forward to Comrade Hu Hanmin in Hong Kong for your review. The violent Japanese invaded the East Province, taking an inch and wanting a foot. The country is in danger, and it is not enough to concentrate the national strength to save it. Comrade has been loyal to the Party and the country, and his words and deeds are cautious and rigorous. He has long been admired by the whole country. He should be invited to enter Beijing immediately to jointly face the national crisis.

Xu Shiying, representative of the Shanghai Charity Organizations Joint Relief Association for Northeast Refugees, said, "Listeners, elders, brothers, sisters, today,

Page 14

Our country's national crisis has reached this point, and it is truly a matter of life and death for the entire Chinese nation. This kind of united, unanimous determination to save the country is enough to show the spirit of our nation, making those who love us happy and those who hate us tremble. Moreover, benevolent soup and righteous grain, accumulated little by little, directly relieve the compatriots in distress, and indirectly save the country. As the saying goes, the people are the foundation of the country, and when the foundation is strong, the country is stable. The association admires the kindness of all walks of life and will first summarize the donations and remit them to Mr. Dong Qu Wenliu and Mr. Feng Yangshan, resident in Pingchang, who will, together with the Deputy Chairman Xiong Xiling, resident in Ping, and entrust Mr. Qi Erdun, the British General Manager of the Qinhuangdao Kailuan Mining Bureau and the Chief Director of the Association, to preside over the relief affairs. We vow to use all the donations, without wasting a penny, on the relief cause. Today, I am publicly pushing Shiying to express my gratitude to you with 120,000 points of sincerity. However, now that the war is not over, the compatriots in distress cannot sleep peacefully for a day, and the mission undertaken by the association cannot be relieved for a day. Regarding all aspects of fundraising and relief, please, listeners, express your opinions and guide us at any time, and ask for tireless goodness and continued donations to save the people and the country. I am extremely grateful. Liang Shiyi's Memorial Service Held Yesterday Morning 105

Hundreds of Dignitaries from All Walks of Life Attended to Pay Tribute

Fundraising for Memorial Items and Scholarship Fund

Liang Shiyi, former Prime Minister, lived in his ancestral home in Guangdong for a long time. He quietly came to Shanghai a month ago and suddenly passed away on the 9th of last month at his residence on Haig Road. Yesterday was the day to receive the posts. Many relatives and friends of Liang Shiyi's lifetime went to pay tribute. Liang's relatives and friends also initiated a fundraising memorial fund to help fund scholarships, and half of the funds have now been collected. The details are recorded below:

Simple Funeral After Liang Shiyi passed away, the coffin was held the next day in accordance with his last wishes. No music was used, no yin-yang masters were used, and there were no underworld instruments or paper crafts, and all things similar to superstition and vanity. Yesterday, the memorial service was held to receive posts. Outside Liang's residence, there was a large shed, with couplets from all walks of life hanging on the four walls. The memorial hall was arranged in the east wing of the house. A sacrificial table was set in the middle, with a censer, several bottles of flowers, and wreaths from relatives and friends. All underworld instruments, sacrificial utensils, and all vulgar customs were eliminated, creating a rather sad and solemn atmosphere.

Tributes from All Walks of Life Yesterday morning, many well-known figures, officials, businessmen from all countries in Shanghai went to pay tribute, including Wu Chaochu, Ye Gongchuo, Mu Ouchu, Qian Xinzhi, Xu Jilun, Li Fuxun, Lin Kanghou, Huang Yanpei, Hu Mengjia, Liu Peiquan, Xu Xinliu, Chen Guangfu, Lu Jianquan, Yang Dunfu, Qu Yingguang, Zhou Zuomin, Wu Yunzhai, Fang Jiaobo, Wang Youling, Wang Binyan, etc. Yesterday was also the day of the public memorial service of the Railway Association. From morning to noon, more than hundreds of people went to pay their respects. Pingjin Bank and all walks of life in transportation also scheduled to hold a memorial service yesterday.

Eulogies from Relatives and Friends Many eulogies were sent from all walks of life. Chiang Kai-shek's memorial text is omitted here because it is too long.

Fundraising for Scholarships Liang's relatives and friends initiated a memorial fund to raise 100,000 yuan first. Currently, there are 33,000 yuan in public bonds, and the number of relatives and friends who have determined the amount and paid cash is about 50,000 yuan. Those who have recognized but not determined the amount are not included. It is said that its use is to edit Liang's Complete Works and subsidize young, poor college students. Each student will receive 500 yuan per year, six in the first year, twelve in the second year, eighteen in the third year, and so on, increasing to forty-two college students in the ninth year. By 1947, the number of students can be expanded to 100. Such a planned scholarship fund is truly worthy of imitation by the Chinese people.

Shanghai Automated Telephone Rate Increase to Take Effect Today 108

Old Rates to Apply to Longhua and Other Areas Without Automated Service

Business Phone Rates to Increase from Six to Ten Yuan

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau under the Ministry of Transportation, after retrofitting to automated telephone service, has decided to increase the rental fees for automatic telephone lines starting May 1st. Although various industry associations jointly opposed the increase, the Telephone Bureau, citing rising gold prices and insufficient revenue to cover expenses, is determined to implement the increase as scheduled. Detailed information is provided below:

▲Notice to the Public The Telephone Bureau's notice states: "To whom it may concern, our bureau's automatic telephone system has begun operation. The equipment was ordered by the Ministry of Transportation from the United States at a total cost of over US$570,000, equivalent to approximately 2,800,000 Chinese yuan. According to the contract, the Bureau must repay US$4,000 per month, equivalent to approximately 20,000 Chinese yuan, from the date of operation. Furthermore, to facilitate rapid and convenient communication for users in the Nanshi and Zhabei districts, we initially intended to lease an additional 100 pairs of trunk lines from the Shanghai Telephone Company. The original annual rental fee for these lines was 50 taels, but the company's newly revised price list sets the annual rental fee at 200 taels per line, a fourfold increase. After repeated negotiations, we were unable to reach an agreement and could only lease 30 pairs. In addition, long-distance and Chinese-administered area calls still require operator assistance, and the costs of materials and parts continue to rise. With the current surge in gold prices and the high cost of living, our existing revenue only covers half of our expenses, resulting in a significant deficit. The Ministry of Transportation, recognizing this situation, has ordered a price increase to help alleviate the financial burden. However, given the economic hardship in Shanghai since the January 28th Incident, we have reduced the proposed prices compared to other areas with automated telephone systems to ease the burden on the public. We will also maintain the old rates for areas without automated service, such as Longhua, Jiangwan, and Zhenru, to further alleviate the burden on citizens. Our difficulties are truly unavoidable. We believe that users and the Bureau have a close relationship, and mutual understanding and cooperation are essential for effective communication. We sincerely hope for your understanding and support. Respectfully, we wish you all the best."

▲Reply to the Chamber of Commerce The Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation sent a letter to the Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: "In response to your letter regarding the Shanghai Restaurant and Catering Industry Association's request to cancel the telephone rate increase, we are writing to provide an explanation. As a state-owned enterprise, we always consider both business development and the financial burden on users. However, the renovation to an automatic telephone system has incurred enormous capital expenditures. We must repay a substantial sum of 20,000 yuan per month, and our total revenues only cover half of our expenses. The deficit is substantial. Following the Ministry's directive, we will slightly increase the rental fees starting May 1st to help alleviate the financial burden. This is an unavoidable measure. Given the economic downturn in Shanghai since the January 28th Incident, the Ministry has adjusted the proposed prices to be lower than the business rates for automatic telephone systems in other areas. Furthermore, areas such as Jiangwan, Zhenru, and Longhua, which will be equipped with automatic systems in the future, will continue to be charged according to the old rates, reflecting our consideration for the public's situation. Therefore, we regret to inform you that we cannot comply with the Restaurant and Catering Industry Association's request to cancel the rate increase. We hope you will understand and inform the association accordingly."

▲New Rate Schedule The new rate schedule of the Telephone Bureau is as follows: (1) Wall-mounted phones: deposit of 50 yuan, installation fee of 20 yuan, monthly rental fee of 7 yuan for Type A and 10 yuan for Type B. Moving fee: 10 yuan within the premises and 20 yuan outside the premises. (2) Desk phones: deposit of 50 yuan, installation fee of 20 yuan, monthly rental fee of 8 yuan for Type A and 11 yuan for Type B. Moving fee same as wall-mounted phones. (3) Extensions: deposit of 50 yuan, installation fee of 10 yuan, monthly rental fee of 3 yuan for both Type A and Type B. Moving fee: 5 yuan within the premises and 10 yuan outside the premises. (4) Branch Exchange: Trunk line deposit of 50 yuan, installation fee of 20 yuan, monthly rental fee of 12 yuan for Nanshi and Zhabei, 15 yuan for Jiangwan, Wusong, Zhenru, Longhua, Nanxiang, and Pudong. Ten-line deposit of 100 yuan, installation fee of 20 yuan. Twenty-line deposit of 150 yuan, installation fee of 30 yuan. Twenty-line deposit of 200 yuan, installation fee of 40 yuan. Twenty-five-line deposit of 250 yuan, installation fee of 50 yuan. Thirty-line deposit of 300 yuan, installation fee of 60 yuan. Fifty-line deposit of 500 yuan, installation fee of 100 yuan. (5) Auxiliary Phones: Bureau phone, deposit of 50 yuan, installation fee of 5 yuan, monthly rental fee of 2 yuan. Moving fee: 5 yuan within the premises, price negotiable outside the premises. For self-provided phones, the deposit and installation fee are waived, and the monthly rental fee is 1 yuan. Moving fee is waived for self-relocation.

Second Special Court Adds Bailiffs 121

| Replacements Drawn from Patrol Police |

When the Jiangsu-Shanghai Second Special District Court was established, it was originally planned to have 16 bailiffs and 4 police chiefs. The General Patrol Bureau was to select capable detectives from various police stations and recommend them for recruitment. Detectives would serve as police chiefs, and Chinese police officers would serve as bailiffs. Later, due to insufficient personnel for dispatch, four additional officers were added, bringing the total to twenty. Recently, due to the large number of criminal cases, the existing number of police officers was still insufficient for deployment. Therefore, the president of the court consulted with the police superintendent of the French Concession and selected six Chinese police officers, numbers 271, 515, 529, 559, 641, and 657, from various police stations to transfer to the court to serve as bailiffs. There are now a total of twenty-six bailiffs, which is sufficient for dispatch, court duty, summoning defendants, and providing bail.

Page 15

Euro-Asia Airlines Long-Distance Test Flight Crashes in Germany 122

Chief of Flight Crew, Schmid, Dies

General Manager Li Jingcong Discusses the Incident Yesterday

The Euro-Asia Airlines long-distance test flight crashed in Germany, the fuselage was completely burned, and the chief of the flight crew, the German Mr. Schmid, died. A detailed account of the incident was obtained from the company's General Manager, Li Jingcong, and is recorded below.

Test Flight Details 123

Our company newly purchased several aircraft in Germany, originally intending to fly them to Shanghai via Russia and Tacheng on the Sino-Russian border at the end of this month (April). However, due to the Xinjiang Incident, this plan had to be postponed to May 8th. Furthermore, since much of the route from Russia to China passes through high mountains and steep ridges, a long-distance test flight was necessary beforehand. Therefore, Mr. Schmid, the chief of the flight crew of our company, was dispatched to conduct a long-distance test flight, including flying over the 3,500-foot-high Alb Mountains, on one of the new aircraft on the afternoon of the day before yesterday (April 29th). Unfortunately, the accident occurred at this time, the fuselage was completely burned, and Mr. Schmid died in the line of duty. The loss of a talent with a historical relationship with our country and Euro-Asia Airlines is deeply regrettable. The details of the cause of the accident have not yet been reported in detail.

History in China 124

Mr. Li continued, "Mr. Schmid came to China in 1927 as a representative of the German Lufthansa, and I (Li referred to himself) negotiated the opening of an aviation business between Europe and Asia in a private capacity. Until the establishment of the National Government, I served as the head of the Aviation Section of the Ministry of Transportation, in charge of aviation matters. Mr. Schmid seized this opportunity to negotiate with me on the Sino-German Euro-Asia Aviation Postal Contract. At that time, there were quite fierce disputes between the two sides regarding rights and interests. Mr. Schmid knew very well that in cooperating with the new China, he could no longer handle this matter from the perspective of previously signed railway cooperation contracts. Finally, with Mr. Schmid's efforts, he was able to adhere to the principle of equality and mutual benefit in all aspects, and the contract was signed in 1929. In 1930, Euro-Asia Airlines (that is, our company) was established, and Mr. Schmid was appointed as the chief of the flight crew. Since the establishment of the company, he has always been involved in every test flight, no matter how difficult or dangerous, just like the test flight on the Shanghai-Manchuria route in the spring of the same year, the test flight on the Shanghai-Xinjiang (via Ruoshui River) route in the winter of 1931, and the test flight on the Shaanxi-Gansu line last spring. The opening of air traffic was also deeply dependent on Mr. Schmid's assistance and planning. I remember that last June, when I left the company, Mr. Schmid made a test flight on the Shanghai-Xinjiang line to Gansu and Xinjiang. He once told me beforehand that all the previous joint test flights had been successful, and this time he felt that there was a sign of difficulty in succeeding on his own. As a result, both test flights failed. In December, I returned to the company as general manager, and it was finally successful. The fate between Mr. Schmid and me is also considered strange. In January of this year, our company, in order to carry out the Euro-Asia inter-air traffic plan, purchased many aircraft in Germany, and specially sent Mr. Schmid back to Germany to preside over the test flight from Germany to China. Mr. Schmid said to me before leaving that he hoped to fly back from Europe together at that time, which would be smoother. Due to official affairs, I was unable to go, and Mr. Schmid sacrificed himself in Germany for long-distance adventurous test flights to promote Chinese aviation and the world aviation business of the Euro-Asia line. No matter what his relationship with me and the future of Chinese aviation, Mr. Schmid's death is a great loss to the aviation industry."

Schmid's Aftermath 125

"I originally planned to fly from Shanghai to Hankou and then to Guangdong the day after tomorrow (3rd) for a test flight on the Guangdong-Hankou line. Now, because Mr. Schmid died in an accident, I have to prepare a memorial service to mark his memory and reschedule it for the 4th. Mr. Schmid's wife is now in Peiping, and I have telegraphed the German Minister to China to notify her. As for Mr. Schmid's bereavement compensation and other aftermath matters, it will be necessary to wait for the Ministry of Transportation to decide on the handling."

Berlin Telegram 126

"Berlin, 29th: A Junkers monoplane of the Sino-German Euro-Asia Airlines crashed to the ground today during a test flight in Traunstein, Bavaria, killing the driver, mechanic, and two passengers. Euro-Asia Airlines manager Schmid was among them, and the fuselage was completely destroyed."

Fiercely Glaring at the Clerk

Strange Photos Discovered After Girl's Death 135

"Da Xin is going to die."

Where do these five words come from?

Da Xin, a seventeen-year-old girl with the surname Chu, residing at No. 68 Ningbo Road in the French Concession, had no prior illness. Sales Promotion of Japanese Trademark Compendium 136

Recruiting 20 Male and Female Salespersons

The Japanese Trademark Compendium, edited by the International Commercial Research Institute, is published by the Publishing Department of the Xinsheng News Agency, located at No. 9 Chongrang Lane, 4th Ma Road in this city. It compiles Japanese trademarks used for products sold in China, categorized into 65 types, including chemicals, pharmaceuticals, paints and pigments, cosmetics, soaps, washing pastes and liquids, metal crafts, silk fabrics, cotton fabrics, wool fabrics, linen fabrics, etc., totaling 1,200 illustrations and 3,000 names. It is a comprehensive collection of Japanese goods and the only reference book for identifying Japanese goods nationwide. The entire book is 400 pages thick, finely printed on Jiangnan Lianshi paper, making the production cost very high. The company, for the sake of popularizing the publication, has set the selling price at $1.50. Since its publication, the book has been ordered by chambers of commerce and anti-Japanese organizations both domestically and internationally as a reference for boycotting Japanese goods. Now, the Xinsheng News Agency, for the sake of broad promotion, has specifically established a method for selling the book, recruiting 20 salespersons in this city, half male and half female, with detailed regulations. Those interested in undertaking this work are requested to send a letter to the company with a one-cent stamp attached before the 10th of this month. The sales regulations will be sent to you. Furthermore, the book has a title inscription by Lin Kanghou, chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, and a preface by Wang Xiaolai, chairman of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, and secretary Yan Esheng, further demonstrating its value.

Record of Ling Kang Wedding Ceremony 138

Wedding Held at the Minglun Hall of the Confucius Temple

Truly Breaking New Ground in Shanghai

|| Words of Mr. Cai Yuanpei ||

Dr. Ling Qihan, director of the Shen Bao Monthly, and Ms. Kang Su, a high-achieving student of the McTyeire School, held their wedding ceremony yesterday at the Minglun Hall inside the Municipal Public Education Center. Guests such as Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Yunhe, Pan Gongzhan, Ma Yinliang, Wang Zhixin, Zhang Yuanruo, Zhang Shutong, Chen Binhe, and Yang Qi, Wang Yongkang, Lu Shidao, etc. from the French Returned Students Association all attended, totaling over two hundred people. Mr. Chen Binhe, representing the guests, delivered a congratulatory speech, and then the ceremony concluded. It is said that Mr. Ling has long intended to reform old customs. Previously, there was no suitable public hall in Shanghai, so people had to hold weddings in small residences or hotels, with solemn ceremonies taking place in undignified venues, which was a regret for the citizens. Therefore, in February, he submitted a document to the Municipal Education Bureau, requesting permission to open the Minglun Hall of the Public Education Center as a public hall. The Bureau approved the request. Therefore, from now on, citizens will not have to worry about not having a solemn and dignified hall for their weddings.

Traveling Thousands of Miles to Hangzhou to Find Her Husband

Lost at the Station, Sent to the Bureau to Await Pickup

Gu Yun Sun, a local resident living at No. 112 Qinyifang, Sipailou, in the city, is over fifty years old. Li Aifen is only 29 years old, and is extremely beautiful. She studied at a certain girls' school. Recently, she started talking nonsense and muttering incessantly. Her family did not take it seriously. Unexpectedly, the day before yesterday, Li, wearing a cheongsam and leather shoes, covered with a yellow Daoist robe, carrying incense candles and paper ingots, boarded the Shanghai-Hangzhou train to Hangzhou alone to offer incense. Unexpectedly, after getting off the train, due to being unfamiliar with the place, she was unable to find her way. So she wandered and looked around at the Hangzhou station. Later, she was spotted by a police officer stationed at the station, who questioned her. Li did not answer the questions asked, and said that she was going to Hong Kong to find her husband, constantly calling Deshan's name. Zhang Juchuan Sues Zhang Huichong for Debt 144

Zhang Huichong, the martial arts film star and former owner of Huichong Film Company, in November 1929, planned to produce the two films "(Love and Hate on the Sea and Sky)" and "(Huang Hai Pirate)", but lacked capital. He asked his brother-in-law Zhang Bingsheng to act as guarantor and borrowed 10,000 yuan from Central Cinema Company, signing a contract stating that after the two films were produced, the income from ticket sales at various cinemas managed by the company should be used to repay the debt. However, after the two films were released, the audience was sparse, and the income from ticket sales was only a little over one-third of the debt, making it impossible to fully repay the debt. On January 29, 1930, Zhang again entrusted Zhang Changfu, the late Chinese manager of Baidai Company, to borrow 2,000 yuan from Central Cinema Company, stating that the previous two films and a new film "(Parricide)" would be screened at the company's cinemas, and the income from ticket sales would be used to repay the debt. Unexpectedly, he repeated the same mistake. To date, apart from the deducted amounts, he still owes 7,306 yuan and 83 cents. Recently, the company found that Zhang was residing in Room 707 of the China Hotel on Guizhou Road. Therefore, manager Zhang Juchuan hired lawyers Zhan Jifeng and Zhan Yigang to sue Zhang and the guarantor Zhang Bingsheng, as well as Zhang Xiaomei (Zhang's daughter), the heir to Zhang Changfu's property, in the First Special Court, requesting Zhang Huichong to repay the amount in full. If Zhang cannot repay it, the guarantor Zhang Bingsheng should repay 5,550 yuan and 83 cents, and Zhang Xiaomei should repay 1,750 yuan, as well as statutory interest and litigation costs. The First Special Court opened a hearing yesterday presided over by Judge Qiao Wanxuan. Because this case has a hope of reconciliation, it was ordered to be rescheduled for further hearing.

Many industrialists and architects have joined and taken on the role of team leader. It is also heard that members of the Menghe Native Place Association will also join the association as a whole.

Minnan: The Shanghai Native Place Association held its 25th executive meeting on the 30th of this month and resolved several important cases. Among the important ones were: (1) The case of how to increase the strength of the Anti-Japanese Vanguard Army. It was resolved to telegraph the anti-Japanese armies of Fujian, Guangdong, and Guangxi to go north and recover the lost territories as soon as possible. (2) The case of how the national masses should enrich the rear support work. It was resolved to send letters to various groups to jointly study and then determine specific methods. (3) The case of how to implement the boycott of enemy goods. It was resolved to assign the investigation to the investigation team. If members of the association are found to have purchased enemy goods, in addition to reporting to the association and publishing a notice to expel them, all anti-Japanese groups across the country will be notified as a disciplinary measure. (4) The case of whether the association's annual publication should be given away for free in addition to distributing it to various members and important groups. It was resolved that anyone who requests it by letter should be given a copy, limited to 100 copies, and other matters will be dealt with in brief.

(2) This competition is temporarily limited to 400 participating children (Yongsheng and Hengsen Radio Stations will each broadcast 200 children). All boys and girls in this city under the age of 15 can participate. Registration starts on May 1st and ends on the 8th. Broadcasting starts on the 12th. (3) This competition designates five registration locations: (1) Yongsheng Radio Station, across from Sincere Company on Nanjing Road, (2) Hengsen Radio Station, Baoanfang, Nanjing Road, (3) Children's Morning News, No. 280 Shandong Road, (4) Children's Entertainment City, China National Products Company, Nanjing Road, (5) Lilih Land Products Company, at the intersection of Zhejiang Road and Tianjin Road. (4) All children participating in the competition must have a parent or adult responsible for taking them to and from the radio station. (5) This competition will assign numbers to the competing children and publish them in advance and notify the competing children, allocating them to Yongsheng and Hengsen Radio Stations equally by date and time. (6) Children's music broadcasting will be broadcast twice a day from May 12th to 22nd. The first time will be on Yongsheng Radio Station, from 2:30 PM to 4:00 PM. The second time will be on Hengsen Radio Station, from 6:45 PM to 8:15 PM. Those who love children's art and are willing to be judges can obtain them from the registration locations listed above. Special Prize: The 50 best performers in each group will be given special prizes. The top three performers will be given special commemorative prizes and photographed for remembrance. (9) This competition also prepares prizes to give to the critics among the listeners. All those whose criticisms match the top three performers (for example, if the top three numbers are 10, 20, and 30, then all those who recognize 10, 20, and 30 as the winners) will be given prizes by this competition to show appreciation. Letters to the Editor 155

To the Editor,

I recently read your newspaper's April 29th article, "The Sichuan Bandits Are Approaching Exhaustion," which mentioned Tian Songyao stopping the offensive and raising funds to suppress the Red Army. This is completely contrary to the facts. Our army has extended the battle line by more than 400 miles since capturing Bazhong and Nanjiang. More than 60,000 troops have been mobilized to encircle and suppress the bandits in a large-scale operation. We have successively occupied key points such as Zhanmao Mountain, Shuangfengchang, Daxueya, Exiangjing, and Yuanbaosi, which belong to Tongjiang County. Tongjiang should be recovered in the short term. The people of the counties in northwestern Sichuan are freely donating funds to reward the army because of our army's efforts to suppress the Red Army. This is witnessed by all. To say that we have stopped the offensive and are raising funds to suppress the Red Army is inaccurate. We are providing a brief account of the situation and request a correction.

Sincerely,

The Resident Office in Nanjing of the 29th Army of the National Revolutionary Army

Weather Report 156

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 pm yesterday stated that the Manchurian low pressure is moving slowly towards the east-northeast. There are strong southerly winds in the Bohai Sea and the northern part of the Yellow Sea. The air pressure over the mainland and the East China Sea is stable, with light southerly winds. The sky is cloudy and humid, and there will be local thunderstorms in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 pm yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 86.2 degrees, and the lowest was 56.3 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 80.6 degrees, and the lowest was 55.9 degrees.

Reader's Consultant

Can the Countryside Really Be Returned To? - A Further Discussion 160

Editor's Note: The discussion on this issue is now coming to an end. This debate originated from two letters from Mr. Xiong Sheng and Mr. You Huaigao, followed by continuous letters from various parties, with seven or eight letters arriving every day. The discussion time has unconsciously extended to such a long time, which we did not expect. From this enthusiastic discussion, we can especially see how important this issue is to us, and how urgently we need to solve this problem. In fact, this is the whole way out for China. At the same time, we are deeply gratified that our readers have participated so enthusiastically in the debate, which shows that the general readers have considerable sympathy for this column. In addition to thanking the letter-writers, this is something we feel deeply comforted by. We originally intended to discuss this issue to a conclusion, but because the time has been extended for so long, and there are many other important letters waiting to be published, we have to announce the end of this discussion halfway. There are still many discussion letters, and the content is very exciting, but they cannot be disclosed. We feel very sorry, and we will publish them separately if there is an opportunity in the future. In this discussion, the focus of the problem is probably on whether it is possible to return to the countryside. The editor's personal opinion is that the focus of this issue is not on whether it is possible to return, but on (1) how to return to the countryside? (2) what to do when returning to the countryside? Therefore, I do not oppose returning to the countryside, but I want to ask what the purpose of returning to the countryside is. If there are correct answers to these two questions, all the secondary disputes can be easily solved. Secondly, in this debate, except for Mr. You Huaigao and Zhu Tianqing, most people said that the countryside cannot be returned to. They have mostly said very thoroughly the reasons why it cannot be returned to, but they have not provided active suggestions on how to remove the reasons why it cannot be returned to.

Even if there is any suggestion, it is very obscure. So there is a group of readers writing to ask: You say that the countryside cannot be returned to, what is your solution? If we do not return to the countryside, where is the way out? In fact, this question is very easy to answer. The first step is to ask whether the current Chinese countryside can be returned to? The answer is no. What is the root cause of why it cannot be returned to? A group of readers has already pointed out the details for me. Then we only need to remove the root cause of why it cannot be returned to, and the countryside can naturally be returned to. Conversely, if we want to return to the countryside, the first thing we can only do is to start by removing the root cause of why it cannot be returned to. There is no other solution. This originally does not need to be explained, since they have already pointed out for us the root cause of why it cannot be returned to, they have already told us the solution on the contrary. For example, in treating a disease, whether it is cold or hot, once the cause of the disease is clear, you only need to prescribe the right medicine. If you need to get to the bottom of it, then that's not very smart. What do you think, readers?

Education News

Special Feature

The Mission of the Sports Meet 162

Luo Jialun

(Written for the Nanjing Four-School Joint Sports Meet)

A sports meet has two meanings:

The first is to promote national health and cultivate a healthy physique.

The second is to cultivate the demeanor of athletes and be a moral model for the nation.

The meaning of the first point is very clear. A healthy mind should reside in a healthy body. Moreover, there are many difficulties and hardships ahead for the Chinese nation. If the emerging generation does not have a persistent and hardworking physique, how can they bear the responsibility of building the country? Great things take time to develop. The success of many great politicians, military strategists,

great scholars, and great entrepreneurs in the world comes after the age of fifty or sixty. However, Chinese people often become old and retire by the age of fifty or sixty. If we do not try to save this situation by developing our physique, what can we imagine for the future of the nation?

The second point is even more important. What I call "the demeanor of athletes" is what ancient China called "the gentleman's competition", and what English calls "sportsmanship". ("A gentleman does not contend for anything. If he must, let it be in archery. He bows and yields as he ascends the platform, and drinks when he descends. His contention is that of a gentleman.") Modern sports have certain rules. According to these rules, in a public place, under the supervision of all eyes, they compete for victory or defeat, without using conspiracies, tricks, or extraneous actions. With their own efforts, they are subject to everyone's public judgment. They are not arrogant when they win, and they do not blame others when they lose. For example, after a tennis match, the winning and losing sides shake hands across the net. Everyone should know that after the US presidential election failed, the loser first sent a telegram to the winner to congratulate him, saying that we both presented our platforms to the people, and the people chose you. I respectfully congratulate you and wish you a smooth success in serving the country. This spirit comes from the sports field. That's different from Chinese politicians who, once they lose power, feel that nothing can be done and use all kinds of conspiracies to sabotage in secret. The reason why Chinese politics is not on track is also because the general public lacks the demeanor of athletes. If Chinese politics and society are to be on track, we must cultivate the demeanor of athletes as the standard of national morality.

A sports meet is not for individuals to compete for trophies. The mission of the sports meet is to cultivate the demeanor of athletes, to coordinate the actions of the group, and to jointly develop a healthy national physique, so that they can jointly shoulder the responsibility of building a new China in the future.

Important News 163

Anhui Provincial Department of Education Prepares for the Entrance Examination 164

The Anhui Provincial Department of Education is actively preparing for the graduation examination for primary and secondary schools. Previously, it appointed several officials from the department and hired a professor from Anhui University to form the First Graduation Examination Committee for Primary and Secondary Schools to prepare everything. It also sent officials to Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hunan, and Hubei to investigate the examination situation. On April 24, the committee held its third meeting. In addition to the members of the preparatory committee, the principals of the provincial capital also attended. First, Zheng Hesheng and Pu Dechao, the investigators sent by the department to Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hunan, and Hubei, reported on the investigation. Then, several resolutions were made as follows: 1. The Standing Committee will draft the method for soliciting examination questions and submit it to the chairman for approval. 2. The number of questions for each examination subject will be doubled. 3. All primary school subjects except composition will use tests. Party principles, history, geography, nature, and foreign languages in junior high school will all use tests. Arithmetic will be tested with propositions, and Chinese will use both tests and propositions. Party principles, geography, and biology in high school will all use tests. Mathematics, physics, and chemistry will all be tested with propositions. Chinese, history, and foreign languages will use both tests and propositions. 4. Stipulate the method of re-examination and describe the difficulties, and submit it to the ministry for approval. 5. The scores of subjects that have not been tested will not be combined. 6. The request from Taiping County Junior High School to exempt English from the examination is not approved. 7. The Finance Department's letter requesting a reduction in the examination budget will be handled by the Standing Committee. 8. The high school examination is scheduled for July 1st to 3rd,

and the primary school examination is scheduled for the 5th to 6th. 9. Announce the high school examination area. 10. The preferential treatment methods for students who pass the examination will be drafted by the Standing Committee and submitted to the meeting for discussion.

▲The first phase opens 300 classes with more than 3,000 students

▲Citizens are eager to study, and it is expected that the number of classes will be increased in the second and third phases After Fujian Province implemented universal literacy education, the survey results showed that the number of illiterate young people exceeded 20,000. Now, the Literacy Committee, in accordance with the planning outline, uses various schools, agencies, and other public places to allocate and supervise illiterate people to study. It has decided to set up 300 classes in the first phase within the possible scope. On the 7th and 8th of this month, the Public Security Bureau of the provincial capital sent students from the police academy to deliver the study notices, ordering them to attend classes on schedule. Those over the age of 25 can also attend classes voluntarily. The textbooks used by the school are

The Literacy Committee has set up two committees, one for editing textbooks and the other for reviewing textbooks, to manage the matter, ensuring that they are practical so that the public can understand and use them in the shortest time. They have been mailed to the Shanghai Commercial Press for zinc plate production, and the content and printing are extremely perfect. The price is also extremely low. Since the opening of the People's School on the 11th, the public has been very enthusiastic about learning. The total number of students in the first phase is more than 3,000. It is expected that the number of classes in the second and third phases will gradually increase in order to accommodate them.

▲And establishes a Science and Engineering Research Institute

The National Beiyang Institute of Technology, formerly Beiyang University, now has three departments: civil engineering, mining engineering, and mechanical engineering. Yesterday, it specifically sent letters to various schools for their information. The original letter is recorded below: Chicken farming is one of the farmer's sideline occupations. Unfortunately, the breeds of chickens are poor, and the feeding methods are inadequate. Those that lay many eggs may not have delicious meat, and those with large bodies may not lay many eggs. To improve the lives of farmers, it is necessary to first seek chicken breeds that are suitable for both eggs and meat. Our center aims to improve chicken breeds and enhance children's interest and ability in production, as well as to inspire children's aspirations and knowledge to improve their lives and agriculture. We plan to conduct trial breeding in schools within this district, which has been approved by the County Education Bureau under directive number 151, and the amended school chicken farming methods have been issued. At this time of the sunny spring, it is the best season for raising chicks. The 189th center affairs meeting of our center designated Zhuanqiao Primary School, Beiqiao Primary School, Jingze Primary School, ZhengGang Primary School, Shangbin Primary School, Yucai Primary School, Dongqiao Primary School, Caoan Primary School, and Xingang Primary School as trial chicken farming schools. We have selected chicks of dual-purpose (egg and meat) breeds and will distribute them to the schools for breeding on May 1st. In addition to informing you, we are sending you the trial school chicken farming methods for your reference and action.

Ministry of Education Edits Methods for Textbooks Used in Primary and Secondary Schools 173

▲ Upon Completion, It May Entrust Book Companies to Print and Distribute

The Executive Yuan meeting on the 25th passed the Ministry of Education's proposal to compile its own textbooks for primary and secondary schools, which has been reported in this newspaper. We now have a copy of the original proposal from the Ministry of Education, which is recorded below:

Regarding the proposal: The textbooks for primary and secondary schools in our country have always been subject to a review and approval system, whereby book companies hire private individuals to edit them, and the government reviews them. After approval, they can be freely published and distributed. This system aims to encourage private writing, so that textbooks can be improved through free competition. However, today, it is also necessary for the government to compile its own textbooks for primary and secondary schools, to be used in parallel with the already approved private works. The reasons are as follows:

1. To Implement National Rejuvenation: National rejuvenation is the key to saving China today. If primary and secondary school textbooks can focus on national rejuvenation, the impact will be profound and related to the future of the nation. However, to rejuvenate the nation, the government must first have a consistent policy, which is more effective when unified and directed by the government. Therefore, primary and secondary school textbooks should be compiled by the government and not merely entrusted to book companies or other private individuals.

2. To Enforce Curriculum Standards: The curriculum standards for primary and secondary schools have been approved by the central government and promulgated by the Ministry of Education. To strictly implement these standards, the government must issue new textbooks that precisely match these standards in order to achieve results. If book companies continue to hire private individuals to edit them, the drawbacks of changing the appearance and plagiarizing old editions will be unavoidable. Even without these drawbacks, there may still be significant differences.

3. To Set an Example for Textbooks: Although there have been improvements in primary and secondary school textbooks in our country over the past thirty years, they have always been edited by private individuals, and the government has not provided active guidance. Therefore, progress has been slow. Although textbooks do not need to adopt a national system, to promote the long-term progress of textbooks, the government should specially compile a set as a demonstration, which is the most effective method of active guidance, far superior to the passive work of simply reviewing and approving them.

Based on the above reasons, the Ministry of Education began preparations last year. In recent months, it has planned to start compiling textbooks for primary and secondary schools for use in primary and secondary schools across the country, and has purchased the latest edited textbooks for primary and secondary schools from Europe, the United States, Japan, and other countries. Several of these have already been translated for reference during the editing process. The proposed implementation methods are described as follows:

1. Types of Textbooks:

A. A complete set of textbooks and teaching materials for all subjects in primary school.

B. A complete set of necessary reference books and wall charts for primary school.

C. A complete set of textbooks for all subjects in secondary school.

2. Those in Charge of Compilation:

A. Primary school textbooks will be handled by the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Education in conjunction with the Compilation and Translation Bureau.

B. Secondary school textbooks will be handled by the National Compilation and Translation Bureau in conjunction with the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Education.

3. Various Textbooks Will Be Completed in Three Phases:

A. Phase 1: Completed by the end of November 1933, published in April 1934.

B. Phase 2: Completed by the end of February 1934, published in July 1934.

C. Phase 3: Completed by the end of August 1934, published in December 1935.

4. Budget.

5. Distribution Method After Completion:

A. The Ministry may entrust book companies to print and distribute them.

B. To be used in parallel with privately compiled textbooks that have been approved by the government.▲ Budget for Compiling Primary and Secondary School Textbooks

Phase 1

(1) Editing 52 volumes of textbooks and teaching methods for elementary primary school Chinese, arithmetic, society, and nature.

(2) Editing 36 volumes of textbooks and teaching methods for advanced primary school Chinese, arithmetic, history, geography, civics, and nature.

(3) Editing 10 volumes of primary school vocabulary, primary school Chinese composition, and French language practice books.

(4) Editing 21 volumes of textbooks for junior secondary school civics, Chinese, arithmetic, Chinese history, Chinese geography, foreign history, and foreign geography.

(5) Editing 23 volumes of textbooks for senior secondary school civics, Chinese, arithmetic, Chinese history, Chinese geography, foreign history, and foreign geography.

Phase 2

(1) Editing 72 volumes of textbooks and teaching methods for elementary primary school hygiene, writing, art, crafts, and music.

(2) Editing 32 volumes of textbooks and teaching methods for advanced primary school hygiene, art, crafts, and music.

(3) Editing 14 volumes of textbooks for junior secondary school English, botany, zoology, chemistry, and physics.

(4) Editing 12 volumes of textbooks for senior secondary school English, biology, chemistry, and physics.

Phase 3

(1) Editing 18 volumes of textbooks for elementary primary school Chinese, society, and nature in a combined Mongolian, Hui, and Tibetan language.

(2) Editing 14 volumes of textbooks for advanced primary school Chinese, history, geography, civics, and nature in a combined Mongolian, Hui, and Tibetan language.

(3) Editing 18 volumes of textbooks for junior secondary school hygiene, crafts, physical education, music, and library science.

(4) Editing 35 volumes of textbooks for senior secondary school hygiene, logic, drawing, music, physical education, Mongolian, Hui, Tibetan, German, Japanese, and Russian languages.

The above totals 142,000 yuan.

Yesterday's Charity Football Match: China Wins 2-1 Against England 175

▲ Both Sides Scored in the First Half

▲ The Game Started Excitingly But Became Dull Later

The Sino-British charity match that caused a sensation in the city was held at Yifu at 3:00 PM yesterday. Approximately ten thousand Chinese and Western spectators, who enjoyed the sport and also supported charitable causes, attended. All proceeds from ticket sales, except for miscellaneous expenses, will be used for charity, and will be jointly handled by the Chinese National Sports Association and the Western Football Association. Both associations will be responsible for reporting the details at that time to ensure fairness. The result of the match was 2-1, with the Chinese team winning.

Xu Shi's Wonderful Kick Breaks the Iron Gate 176

The English team applied pressure from the start, with five lines of troops invading in different directions. The strong central defense line formed a encirclement, and the Chinese team was flustered and trapped in the circle. At this time, Chen Zhenhe, who had been away from the field for a long time, was unanimously supported. He wiggled his feet and dribbled the ball out of danger, boosting the morale of the team. Li Yichen and Sun Jinshun advanced side by side, and in the blink of an eye, the English goal was in sight. Unfortunately, it was ruled offside. Seeing that the enemy's momentum was still strong, Li Te went down the right wing, passing to the center. Hai Te Lai skillfully dodged Wang Shusen, using a trick under his feet, taking advantage of the other's unpreparedness and passing to the left. Left winger Xu Shi was waiting for orders. A ball came across, and he fell forward and shot, hitting the net in response. It was a beautiful goal, and the iron gate, like Zhou Xianyan, could do nothing about it.

Yu Tian's Clever Plan Captures the Enemy's Pass 177

After losing a goal, the Chinese team reorganized its formation, hoping to recover. Tu Kaiyuan took a long-range free kick, which was caught by Brett Lai with a jump, turning it into a corner kick. Wan Xianghua shot accurately, and in the crowd of figures, Chen Jiaqiu secretly sent a foot, inches away from the goal. An interesting thing suddenly happened. From the left side outside the penalty area of the English goal, the Chinese team got a free kick. Chen Yutian was going to execute it, but the ball suddenly deflated. He changed to an old ball, but it was also unsuitable. He changed to another ball. At this time, Chen Yutian secretly sent a wink, and Tu Kaiyuan responded with a smile. Electric waves were transmitted to each other, and they understood each other. A kick came over, and Tu Kaiyuan stepped forward and shot, hitting the net and tying the score. Five minutes later, the Wan-Sun-Li triangle alliance collapsed the enemy's fort. Sun Jinshun lived up to his mission and returned victoriously. In the first half, China took the lead 2-1.

Gai Xu Fails to Score on Penalty Kick 178

The Western front had been quiet for a long time, and the strong men felt like they were developing fat on their thighs. They had no choice but to shorten each half of the first half by thirty minutes to remedy this. The situation in the second half turned dull. After ten minutes, Wang Shusen was penalized for saving the day, and a penalty kick was awarded. Zhou Xianyan rubbed his fists, preparing to resist. Captain Gai personally executed the kick, but he kicked it out diagonally, intentionally giving up, or perhaps he missed the target. It is unknown. Afterwards, the time passed in a playful manner. Both sides shot as soon as they got the ball, regardless of its effectiveness. Towards the end, it became more and more lax. Generally, the winner had no intention of trying again, and the loser was also confident that the hard work would be futile. The referee gave the order to retreat, and both sides returned to their teams in an orderly manner. The result was 2-1, with China winning. Referee Ai Quexun, linesmen Li Silian and Shen Huichun.
