A Brief Overview of Medicine and Pharmaceuticals in Shanghai Over the Past Decade (Continued) 187

— Pang Jingzhou

Chapter 4: Business Conditions

(B) The Business of New Medicines

I have proposed to the Physicians' Association to form another committee to properly organize the new drug catalog, publications, and explanations. It has been passed, but so far very little work has been done. I will write another article about the methods and opinions another day.

Under the current situation, the most important thing is naturally the pharmaceutical factory. Although most of the chemical raw materials are still imported, the imitation and preparation can still block some loopholes. It is a pity that there are only four or five such pharmaceutical factories in Shanghai, such as New Asia, Shinyi, and Fukang. The capital is still insufficient, and the products are not very abundant. Moreover, the psychology of worshiping foreign goods cannot be avoided from the patient's side to the doctor's side. Therefore, the business of pharmaceutical factories is not very developed. This matter needs to be promoted by the society.

Shanghai can be said to be the largest market for new medicines in the country. Even the medicines used by hospitals and doctors in various parts of the interior are supplied by these ten or so Cheng Le merchants, twenty or so formula merchants (also engaged in wholesale), five or six pharmaceutical factories, and a part of the larger foreign pharmacies (small pharmacies opened by Russians in the city have no ability to promote medicines to the interior), and several resident managers of foreign pharmaceutical factories. In total, the number of merchants is less than half of the old-fashioned Chinese medicine shops in Shanghai (exclusively selling in this city). Although the northern provinces are supplied by Tianjin, Qingdao, and other places, the abdominal provinces are supplied by Hankou, the Yunnan and Guizhou provinces are imported from Saigon, and the Guangdong medicines are imported from Hong Kong, either they are still Shanghai branch offices, or there are not many shops. All have factual evidence that can be investigated. From the north, it can be proved that the total number of medical equipment and medicines that our country relies on from foreigners is not surprising. The cause of new medicine is not developed at all. However, now the general advocacy of preserving old medicine often takes the outflow of rights and interests and the language of promoting domestic goods to sensationalize. The government officials also think that (scientific medicine should be promoted, but the leakage of Western medicines is too great, so it is better to cut your feet to fit your shoes and open Chinese medicine halls. But on the one hand, they rely on the American wheat, cotton, Saigon rice, German rayon, and all the necessities of daily life from foreigners, but they do not consider it very much and say (promote national agriculture). (Promote the national quintessence of sericulture)? Alas! Giving up the root and pursuing the branches, what is going on? (End of this section)

How to Maintain Good Health (Part 2) 188

— Sun Huajun

(1) How can we avoid the occurrence of infectious diseases?

Infectious diseases are the greatest enemies of health and life. Preventing them from entering the body and causing illness is the primary condition for protecting health. We know that the cause of infectious diseases is bacteria. They must invade our bodies to cause illness. If we can cut off their path of invasion, the disease will not occur. The paths of invasion are: (1) Transmission through food, entering the stomach and intestines through the mouth, such as typhoid fever, cholera, dysentery, and intestinal parasites. The prevention method is to avoid eating raw water and raw vegetables, especially in summer, and not to eat cold food that flies have landed on, as well as spoiled food. Do not use the tableware used by patients, and pay attention to disinfecting patients' feces and urine. (2) Transmission through the air, entering the lungs through the nose, such as pulmonary tuberculosis, pneumonia, plague, and influenza. The prevention method is to stay away from patients, keep a distance of at least five feet when talking, and do not use tableware used by patients. Diphtheria enters the body through the mouth or nose. (3) Transmission through contact between bodies via viruses, such as venereal diseases and scabies. The prevention method is to stay away from unclean women, and not to have sexual relations with suspicious women. If it is unavoidable, use protective devices such as condoms or "Ruyi bags." If problems arise, see a formal doctor early to avoid being beyond remedy. (4) Entry into the body through skin wounds via viruses, such as various suppurative diseases and anthrax. Therefore, when the skin is broken, attention should be paid to disinfection. (5) Transmission through bites of animals via viruses, such as mosquitoes for malaria, fleas for plague, and mad dogs for rabies. The prevention method is simply to isolate such animals. For example, mosquito nets can prevent mosquitoes, and long boots can prevent fleas. Such prevention should be handled according to the situation at any time and in any place.

(2) How can we strengthen the body and increase resistance?

The resistance of our body is an essential element of health, the driving force for resisting disease. Everyone should pay attention to and improve it to make the body stronger. Many people believe in getting blood-boosting injections and taking supplements to achieve this goal, but this is a mistake. Natural sunlight, fresh air, and light are the real tonics. Gentlemen, do not think this is just old-fashioned talk. These three treasures can not only strengthen the body, but also are good medicine for treating lung diseases. Don't you see how strong and energetic the Germans are? Their secret is to use these three treasures. We Shanghai people live in the city, our houses are as small as pigeon nests, our lives are unstable, our habits are bad, and we lack these three substances, resulting in pale complexions and listless spirits. Why not make an effort to absorb these real tonics that cost nothing? As long as people exercise in fresh air for half an hour every day and see the sunlight, I guarantee your body will be stronger than taking medicine and injections. As for exercise, we do not advocate doing strenuous competitive sports such as running and playing ball, because they are harmful to the body. The best are flexible exercises or Tai Chi, because the movements of the muscles are even and do not harm the heart and lungs. The most important thing is not to interrupt. This ultraviolet light is especially useful for busy people. Exposing yourself to the sun for at least ten minutes a day will definitely make your body healthy and beautiful.

However, exercise cannot be excessive. It is especially unsuitable for people with heart and lung diseases, otherwise the problem will worsen. Exposure to sunlight and ultraviolet light is not necessarily good. For example, people with lung disease and fever, and some people with skin diseases, cannot be exposed to it. So, how can it be considered complete? We can say that all people who want to obtain health and maintain health cannot be separated from the management and guidance of doctors.

Advice to Those Suffering from Venereal Diseases (Part 2) 189

— Hu Jiayan

(4) In addition to using slogans of cheapness and good quality to attract customers, they are also afraid that patients are not at ease, so they came up with a kind of policy to explain that if it is not cured or not fully cured by the due date, the diagnosis fee can be refunded, etc. They even say that they can use the health bureau's verification form as proof. Of course, anyone can listen to this kind of talk, but is it really the case? We know that the spread and cessation of any disease is sometimes very unpredictable, and it is not exactly the same as the fixed model said in books; and every disease has the possibility of developing other complications (even mild diseases are the same). Although it is said that various methods can be used in advance to prevent it, it is not always possible in reality. Venereal diseases are no exception, so it is not possible for a doctor to guarantee a full recovery when diagnosing a disease. Although he may see many cases get better. As for the insurance policy, there is no need to mention it! Even if we take a step back, since this matter is voluntary, it is inconvenient for others to criticize. Then I might as well explain a few more words to the patient about the verification form. Regarding the general rules of verification, only positive numbers (i.e., addition, meaning existence) have value in theory, and negative numbers (i.e., subtraction, meaning non-existence) have little value. For example, if a person's Wassermann reaction is negative, then we cannot say that he is definitely free of syphilis now, or even that he has been completely cured; the same is true for the absence of gonorrhea bacteria in the examination of leucorrhea, and the absence of tuberculosis bacilli in the sputum of tuberculosis. Positive numbers are easy to get when the symptoms are obvious, but not so for latent ones. By the time syphilis reaches the third stage (brain syphilis and spinal cord sputum), the clinical diagnosis is very reliable, but the blood test is not necessarily positive: when leucorrhea develops into unilateral arthritis, if his urethra has no changes, then no cocci can be found. If the patient goes to question him at this time why he has not been completely cured, he can take the verification form as his defense, what else can you say! The clever ones, of course, say that you have another disease, and his treatment of sputum is not the same as before, and you are not clear about it. Even if the examination is not negative, they can casually point out a small section of your daily life, saying that it was caused by your carelessness (we have always had a saying that when urinating, you will get turbid pain if you are suddenly exposed to cold wind; many people believe this, and there are many similar cases, so they can of course point it out casually). Or they may even say that you are newly infected. What can you argue! Moreover, five or six out of ten patients with venereal diseases are deeply reluctant to talk about it, and Chinese people are naturally inclined to avoid trouble and not be too demanding; even if there is really something wrong that is seen, no one will bother to do anything. So their tricks will never be exposed.

Based on the above circumstances, the following two general rules can be discovered, namely, the easier the diagnosis, the less reliable it is; the more exaggerated the advertisement, the more careful you should be; I will explain these two separately below:

(1) This one is probably very easy to cause misunderstanding. Because diagnosis is sometimes not easy, but sometimes you only need to rely on a clinical examination to know the general situation. There is also a lot of evidence for this, but taking venereal diseases as an example, the diagnosis is not very difficult for the initial stage of acute leucorrhea, when syphilis occurs in the whole body, and when the symptoms of spinal cord sputum are obvious. But I am completely speaking for a reason. Because most of these doctors do not have a real foundation in medicine, their knowledge is half from fixed books and half from hearsay. They know what is natural but do not know why, they know the model venereal disease type but do not know the various variations; so their diagnosis and treatment of diseases only have arbitrary mistakes, and there will be no hesitant places, which is conceivable. Furthermore, they are timid and afraid of being exposed, if they cannot report a disease for a while, they are afraid that the patient will not feel at ease, so this kind of mistake is the easiest for them to make.

(2) I am definitely not saying that doctors' advertisements should not be published, but I do not approve of exaggerated and overly deceptive propaganda! This is also what they are used to, and they can almost take care of everything; in addition to newspapers and regular daily, weekly, and monthly publications, there are also various innovative slogans on the clinic's door and window glass, just like a newly opened theater or restaurant. This is their only sign. People who have lived in Shanghai for a long time probably already know the truth; but there are still many people who come from other places and are deceived. So I also do not mind being trivial and put it forward to remind patients to pay attention.

The things that patients should pay attention to when seeking medical treatment, I have written all that I know! Of course, this kind of situation is definitely not limited to the venereal disease part, but it is undoubtedly true that it accounts for the majority. In addition, I have a few things that I hope patients themselves will pay attention to:

(1) The period of relief from the pain of venereal diseases is sometimes not very difficult, and the time is not long, but complete recovery and prevention of future complications are not simple, and the treatment time is also very long; it is definitely not the case that you can count on it just because you feel that your body has no major pain or one examination report. Chronic leucorrhea is especially stubborn and difficult to cure. Therefore, patients must not be too impatient, and temporary gains and losses are not very important: definitely do not be optimistic because of short-term treatment that is slightly effective, and vice versa.

(2) Patients should pay attention to the choice of doctors before seeking medical treatment; but after the choice has been made, the decision must be firm.

Page 18

It is absolutely impossible to change the plan because of temporary small gains and losses, which is harmful and not beneficial.

(3) Patients often seek medical treatment through proper methods during diagnosis and treatment, but if they do not see immediate results, they seek medical treatment from other doctors. However, if other doctors diagnose that the previous treatment method was correct and the plan was the same as before, they are often not happy. They even ask the doctor to change other methods. This kind of psychology of excessively valuing novelty is of no benefit to the disease itself.

(4) Patients often like to participate in opinions during diagnosis, and even seek medical treatment on the one hand, and use their own legendary methods on the other hand. As a result, they get into trouble and seek trouble for themselves, so they should pay special attention.

(2) Appendix

During childbirth, the delivery room should have medical equipment, all of which are prepared by the obstetrician. It is not necessary to repeat this here. The items that the family should prepare are listed below:

Sheets, oilcloth or oil paper, gauze, cotton, bathtub, clothes for the baby and the mother, large towels, small towels, belly wrap, safety pins (in large quantities), cold water, boiling water, etc.

The midwife should check and record the newborn and its appendages:

(1) Infant body: Number of fetuses delivered: alive or dead, gender, weight, height

Head measurements: fontanelles, sutures, birth tumors, etc.

Overall development status: any deformities

(2) Umbilical cord: thickness, length, gelatinous substance, development status, nodules, etc.

(3) Amnion: size of rupture, shape, location, etc.

(4) Placenta: weight, shape, size, thickness, any defects or accessory placenta, etc.

Monster Fetus

Li Xiaofu is a coppersmith, living at No. 4, Xiezhen Lane, Zhongxing Road, Zhabei. His wife, Ms. Lu, is 28 years old and from Wuxi. She became pregnant last year, her fourth pregnancy. Labor started at 4:00 AM on December 29th last year. At 1:00 PM, the midwife Wang Jiangshi, who had been hired, forcibly pulled out the baby's head. At 5:00 PM, she pulled out the baby's hand, but the entire fetus was still difficult to deliver. Therefore, Li Xiaofu sent the pregnant woman to the Sino-German Obstetrics and Gynecology Hospital on Zhangjiabang Road, Jing'an Temple Road in this city. She was admitted to the hospital at 11:00 PM. The hospital's doctor then used surgery to remove the entire fetus, only to find that it was a deformed baby of the hydrops fetalis type (see attached picture). The neck was thin and long, the abdomen was as big as a drum, the limbs were soft, the tissue was incomplete, and the genitals had eight testicles, which was unprecedented. The whole body was scarred, caused by the midwife's reckless pulling. It is now reported that this deformed fetus has been taken by the Academia Sinica for research, and a report will be available soon.

Common Knowledge Q&A About Diseases (7) 191

— Cheng Hanzhang

▲ Malaria

Q: How does malaria start?

A: It is caused by a type of sporozoan parasite that lives inside blood cells.

Q: How can malaria sporozoans invade the human body's blood?

A: Because this sporozoan parasite first lives in the stomach of a type of mosquito (called an Anopheles mosquito), when the Anopheles mosquito sucks blood, it enters the human blood along with the mosquito's saliva.

Q: Does this disease have other names?

A: There are vulgar names such as "San Yin Malaria," "Cold and Heat Disease," and "Hitting the Board," and there is also the alternative name "Intermittent Fever."

Q: What is the Western name?

A: Malaria, also known as Febris intermittens. In German, it is also called Wechselieber.

Q: Where and in what season is malaria most common?

A: It occurs a lot in the tropics and in the south of our country. It is more common in spring and autumn than in winter.

Q: How many days does it take to develop the disease after we are infected with malaria sporozoans?

A: It takes ten to fourteen days to develop the disease.

Q: What are the main symptoms of malaria?

A: Periodic intermittent fever.

Q: Is this intermittent period fixed?

A: There are those that occur every other day, called tertian fever; those that occur every two days, called quartan fever; and there are also those that are irregular and dangerous, called malignant malaria or tropical malaria.

Q: What are the symptoms of tertian fever and quartan fever?

A: Mostly, a sudden onset of severe chills and shivering, pale face, cold skin, and small pulse occur first, then the body temperature rises, and the skin becomes hot. After this, the pulse becomes fuller and faster, and the spleen swells up. In addition, there are complaints of limb pain, nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, crawling rash on the face, and hypersensitivity of the skin. Finally, sweating occurs and the fever subsides. On average, the body temperature returns to normal in six to ten hours. (To be continued)

What is (Sha Medicine Water)? As the name suggests, this is certainly a liquid for treating Sha symptoms. However, the (Sha Medicine Water) that the general public recognizes now is not so simple. The term (Sha Medicine Water) does include (Ten Drops Water), (Life-Saving Water), (Universal Relief Water), (Benefit-the-Public Water), (Miraculous Benefit-the-Public Water):: etc., etc., many waters. I can't count them all at once. Although the instructions state what diseases it treats, how to take it, and how much to take each time, the general public often does not pay attention to it. They even regard this kind of (Sha Medicine Water) as a (universal) (elixir). It seems that no matter what symptoms there are, it is okay to use it, and it really has the effect of (curing the disease with medicine) and (bringing the dead back to life). Such excessive trust in (Sha Medicine Water) even makes people think that it is an essential treasure for (home and travel). In fact, they simply don't understand what (Sha Medicine Water) is made of, what its function is!

The preparation of Sha Medicine Water is roughly composed of (cardiotonic) and (sedative) drugs. Because it has the function of strengthening the heart, it can be used to urgently rescue all cases of syncope caused by severe vomiting, diarrhea, excessive labor, accidental stimulation, etc. And because it has a sedative effect, it can also stop vomiting and diarrhea, relieve pain, and inhibit cramps and spasms.

What I have to explain to you is that the effect of cardiotonic drugs is threefold: (1) to inhibit excessive excitement of myocardial contraction; (2) to promote the function of myocardial contraction. The effects of the two are contrary to each other, and there are many differences in the application. However, the functions of the two can sometimes complement each other. This is certainly not something that this article can fully explain in detail. If the cardiotonic drugs in Sha Medicine Water mostly have both functions, they certainly have an effect when applied to mild or non-serious heart failure. (In severe heart failure, paralysis is too severe, and oral medicine rarely works.) However, when used in excess, the heart cannot bear the stimulation. Excessive excitement is really enough to make the heart dysfunctional and endanger life. It is like drinking alcohol. Drinking a little can indeed stimulate the activity of the myocardium and increase blood circulation, and you often feel physically and mentally comfortable. Overdoing it will get you drunk, and drunk you will be crazy. This is still in the transition period of excitement and paralysis. In an instant, from madness to sleep, sleep and sound sleep, even unconscious. This is because it has shifted from the excitement period to the anesthetic state, resulting in excessive excitement, causing cerebral congestion or blood vessels to burst and die. There are also many real cases of sudden syncope due to excessive heart palpitations and exhaustion. Therefore, it is said that (too much is as bad as too little), and the disaster may be even worse.

The effect of sedatives is that they can stop vomiting and diarrhea, relieve pain and inhibit spasms, as mentioned earlier. Therefore, this type of drug mostly contains (narcotics). It has the function of inhibiting nerve excitement; it has special effects on anesthetizing peripheral nerves or central nerves. They all belong to (powerful drugs) or (toxic drugs). When used properly, they work quickly. When used improperly, they can endanger life. Even if it doesn't kill you, there are often many side effects. Please set an example to illustrate its generality.

(Opium) is enough to help increase energy, which is its stimulating effect on the nerves. At the same time, it also has a pain-relieving effect, which is also its anesthetic effect. Anyone who has ever smoked opium to relieve pain can tell you about it. Those who smoke more than one tube often find that although the pain is relieved, they feel dizzy, dry mouth, nausea and upset, which is also called (seeking benefit but getting loss). However, this is still not enough to endanger life. If opium is used as an oral or injectable agent, without following the regulations, there are few who are not poisoned. Opium's anesthetic effect is especially harmful to the central respiratory nerves. Once breathing stops, the source of oxygen is cut off. Even if the heart is not weak, what good is it? Those who enter in this way are close to the underworld!

Recently, various (Sha Medicine Water) sold in shops. The formulations are certainly numerous. There must be many who mix (opium wine) or (opium smoke water). There are even those who use (pet heads water) as medicine and mix it with wine agents or water and wine to become what is called Sha Medicine Water, which is certainly not completely without harm. Many people have not noticed it. There are many types of Sha Medicine Water, and the formulations are different. However, in my opinion, it is nothing more than the aforementioned two types of drugs combined. There are also those who use prescriptions from old Chinese medicine and mix them with Western medicine, which is something I dare not discuss. However, I have seen people who excessively trust Sha Medicine Water and are harmed by misuse, and I feel sorry and worried about it! Now I will briefly give a few examples to illustrate it.

(1) A certain merchant woke up in the morning with a slight abdominal pain. Fearing that he had Sha symptoms, he took the specially prepared (Sha Medicine Water) and drank it, and the pain stopped. After about two hours, the pain recurred. He took Sha Medicine Water again to treat it, but it didn't work, so he drank more of it, and after a while, the pain began to subside. However, he felt deeply troubled and didn't know how to feel better. He went on to rub and scrape it, and red Sha clearly appeared around his neck and chest and back. He thought that the Sha root had been removed and the disease was okay. However, the abdominal pain came again in no time, even worse than before. Panicked and crying out in pain, he took Sha Medicine Water again and drank it, half a bottle without effect, then another half a bottle. The pain did not decrease, and he vomited non-stop, bringing up all the food from the previous night, but still not stopping. He sweated and breathed quickly, his hands were cold and cramped, the pain was even more intense, and his condition was critical. He was rushed to the hospital. Upon questioning, the above-mentioned statement was obtained. In total, he took about three bottles of Sha Medicine Water in four hours. After examination, there were already signs of poisoning. And the so-called main symptom was that he had been constipated for four days. He had first felt abdominal pain the other day and relied entirely on Sha Medicine Water to cure it. So they washed his stomach to clear the remnants of Sha Medicine Water, and his intestines to clear his stool. After the stool was passed, the disease was indeed cured immediately. This is truly what is called (There is nothing wrong in the world, fools trouble themselves)!

(What would have happened if this merchant had not vomited after taking Sha Medicine Water for the third time?) It must be said that (it would have been bad). However, people attribute the merchant's good fortune in not dying to vomiting. In fact, the reason for his rescue was not only this. If the so-called (Sha Medicine Water) he took was (Ten Drops Water), its dose was strong, and the anesthetic it contained might have caused the taker to be incurable early on? Fortunately, the Sha Medicine Water he took was not very strong, and because it was separated by some time, it was not very dangerous: he saw the opportunity early and sought medical treatment immediately: and he was able to directly admit that he had taken a large amount of Sha Medicine Water, avoiding wasting the doctor's examination. If the Sha Medicine Water he took was not vomited out, because of the excessive dose, he would have entered a state of drunkenness. By the time others discovered it, they could not prove whether he had taken Sha Medicine Water or other drugs; or even if he had been given it by others, he would conceal and avoid fault, and would not be willing to speak. Doctors will encounter a lot of trouble. Even if there are slight symptoms of poisoning, they must pay attention to it. After showing the effect, it is necessary to advise the patient not to follow the same path.

Free Talk

On Foreign Bagu 192

— Xuan

Where there is "country," there is "foreign." With domestic bagu, there is naturally so-called foreign bagu.

Domestic bagu is a means for emperors to unify thought. Similarly, ancient and modern crowned and uncrowned emperors in foreign countries have the same trick. In contrast to domestic bagu, that is foreign bagu.

This is one explanation of foreign bagu. It can also be said to be the original meaning of foreign bagu.

Since maritime trade opened, foreign goods have been imported into China, followed by disrupting China's original socio-economic organization. Thus, domestic bagu lost its function and had to beg for help from foreign bagu. Thus, we have foreign bagu here. This kind of foreign bagu is meant to replace domestic bagu to (correct people's hearts and resist heresies). For example, fascism is the latest foreign bagu.

Foreigners also have other bagu. For example, in places where fascism does not work well, there is social democracy, a type of foreign bagu. China is a complex country, so some people have imported this foreign bagu, although sales have not been very smooth.

In addition, Kemal of Turkey and Gandhi of India are both (bagu masters;) their bagu is a different style, but their convergence with orthodox foreign bagu (different paths to the same destination) is already a widely seen effect. Therefore, we have also put up big advertisements for them in our market.

Foreign bagu also has two proud writing styles: anesthesia and deception. Although these are (unorthodox), their power is no less than that of a frontal direct approach. Domestic bagu also had this kind of trick, but it is never as good as foreign bagu in researching these to infinite variations and unpredictable wonders. And judging from recent facts, our foreign bagu students are not weaker than their teachers in these two aspects!

Now the Washington Conference is about to open. Maybe there will be an amazing foreign bagu, we'll wait and see!

Foreign bagu has other explanations, but that is not within the topic today, we will talk about it when we have the opportunity in the future.

Father and Daughter 193

— Zhang Xuezhen

In the past two or three years, during the rainy seasons of summer and autumn, whenever we had a broken umbrella at home, my mother would tell me to take it out to be repaired. I would habitually run to Wang Shun's umbrella repair shop! Calling it a shop might be an exaggeration; it was just a dark little room. The counter had become smooth and shiny from years of being touched.

(Shopkeeper, please fix this umbrella for me.)

(Alright), an old man would put down the work in his hands with a smile and stand up to greet his customer with a unique warmth. Seeing his white hair fluttering and his forehead full of wrinkles, I figured he must be sixty years old.

His attentiveness and warmth made us familiar with each other.

Every day, on my way to and from school, I would glance into the shop. I saw his hunched silhouette, so engrossed in his work, as if his life, his joy, were bound up in the hemp thread and oiled paper.

(Going to school? So early!) He would smile, twisting his beard when he happened to look up and see me. He was often so diligent that he forgot his fatigue, working from early morning until late in the evening without rest.

(Where do you study? It's a pity my A-Yun didn't have the good fortune. She's very clever and knows a few characters too…)

(Dad, aren't you ashamed, always bragging like that.) A-Yun blushed. A pretty figure, tall, with a slightly dark complexion, and bright pupils that seemed to capture one's soul, she was a quiet young woman.

(A-Yun's mother died six or seven years ago. That's our hard luck. Fortunately, the neighbors are good and treat us like family, otherwise, it would be too lonely.)

(Shopkeeper, how's business?)

(It's uncertain. Business is good when it rains, but it's common for no one to come for ten days or half a month.)

(You repair them well; your craftsmanship is really good. I'll spread the word and tell people to come to you.) I examined the repaired umbrella. He was so capable that he fixed it like new.

(Oh, no, if there are too many, I won't be able to fix them in time, and failing to deliver on time is a bad thing.) He frowned and said, (Ah, if A-Yun's mother were alive, she was very good at repairing them. You never saw that good woman; I can't forget her kindness even for a day…)

(What is it, Dad? Don't mention those sad things again. Mom is dead; are you sure she's okay with you being this upset?) I looked at her face, deeply saddened. A small black mole on her forehead made her even more charming. Two crystal tears were in her eyes.

(That's true, money and people are gone. Fortunately, A-Yun is older now. A-Yun can help you do some work, right?)

(She can't do that forever. She's eighteen years old now, it's about time…) A-Yun ran over to cover her father's mouth. It was summer, and a pink plaid short jacket made her even more beautiful.

Today, as I walked past with my schoolbag, I was stunned to see a white curtain hanging in front of the shop. I remembered the umbrella I had just taken there the day before, and I stepped into the shop.

A-Yun came out of the mourning hall wearing mourning clothes, her eyes swollen like lychees, her hair like a pile of messy firewood.

(What happened? Who?) Actually, besides her father, who else could it be?

(Dad said he wasn't feeling well a couple of days ago, but I didn't pay attention. Who knew that yesterday he vomited and had diarrhea, and he passed away at noon today,) she sobbed, (Heaven, how can I go on?)

I couldn't find a word to comfort her. This seemed to be A-Yun's inevitable fate.

A-Yun looked at me forlornly as I walked out, her eyes red. I forgot about the umbrella.

Watermelon Seeds and the Chinese Nation 194

— Wen Juan

It is said that when a certain Chinese actor was performing in the United States, on the first day, there were indeed many American audience members. However, the impression of the watermelon seed shells scattered all over the floor by the Chinese audience members sitting with them frightened them. So, on the second day, only watermelon seed shells and the Chinese people who created those watermelon seed shells remained in the theater; there were no American audience members to be seen.

Alas! The power of watermelon seeds is so great and far-reaching! This is already the case in faraway foreign countries, let alone within our own country! We don't need to mention anything else; just take Shanghai as an example. From wealthy people living in Western-style houses to the so-called (peddlers and laborers), almost every family has traces of watermelon seeds every day. Guests at banquets need watermelon seeds, and even people chatting idly at the door of small houses have watermelon seeds in their hands. I often think: if someone were to calculate the total amount of watermelon seeds consumed in China every day and the amount of time wasted by watermelon seeds, they would certainly obtain an astonishing number!

Looking at the nationwide addiction to eating watermelon seeds, we can see how many idle and unemployed people there are in China! Because the greatest purpose of eating watermelon seeds is to kill time and relieve boredom. Not only during ordinary times but even in the most intense meeting rooms and movie theaters, we Chinese are still bored and idle, and watermelon seeds are still needed to drive away loneliness. Therefore, it seems that an inseparable relationship has been established between the Chinese people and watermelon seeds.

Moreover, the appearance of watermelon seeds can symbolize the demeanor of our great Chinese people. The Chinese people's disorganization and lack of unity, the strong individualistic tendencies, the antagonism and infighting within individual China, the willingness to be defeated by foreigners one by one rather than compromise with each other—are these not exactly the same as the watermelon seeds we eat every day?

Ramblings from Mai Lu 195

— Zi Zhan

(Twenty-three) National Martial Arts and Foreign Aggression

During the late Qing Dynasty, when governance was lost and foreign troubles deepened, after experiencing much hardship and suffering many insults, the idea of using spiritual boxing to resist foreign aggression arose. This was the origin of the Boxer Rebellion. Since the Japanese invaders came, everyone has been clamoring for resistance. Airplanes and cannons are far inferior to the enemy; but using broadswords can occasionally achieve miraculous results, which the Chinese people greatly exaggerate. Recently, Han Fuju, Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, specifically decided to hold a provincial national martial arts examination starting on May 14th to seek out talents with extraordinary abilities in flying, roaring, running, leaping, and acupressure. He will provide equipment, prepare prizes, and treat them with the respect due to honored guests. Moreover, he does not limit applicants by province or qualifications; anyone can come to demonstrate their skills. (See this newspaper's issue from the 20th of last month.) When foreign aggression awaits resistance, national martial arts will flourish. Historical books are full of examples of this. The History of the Han Dynasty, Biography of Wang Mang, says that in the sixth year of the Beginning Founding, Wang Mang widely recruited people with extraordinary skills who could attack the Xiongnu, intending to give them unprecedented positions. Tens of thousands of people claimed to have useful skills. Some said they could cross water without boats or rafts, linking horses and riders to transport a million troops. Some said they could go without grain or food, taking medicine so that the entire army would not be hungry. Some said they could fly a thousand miles a day, spying on the Xiongnu. Wang Mang tested them all, taking large crows and attaching two wings to them, covering their heads and bodies with feathers, and attaching rings and buttons. They flew several hundred steps and fell down. Wang Mang knew they were unusable, but he still wanted to enhance their reputation, so he made them military commanders and awarded them carriages and horses. It can be seen that when the country was in crisis during Wang Mang's time, he wanted to use airplanes to spy on the enemy, and already had the idea of aerial warfare. It is a pity that this national martial art has been lost and could not be carried forward. Otherwise, as of today, there would be domestic aircraft to resist the Japanese invaders. The History of the Song Dynasty, Biography of Sun Fu, says that when the Jin people surrounded the capital, Fu personally defended the city day and night. Reading the poem "Feeling Events" by Qiu Jun, which has the line "(Guo Jing deceived Liu Wuji)," Fu found Wuji among the common people in the market and found Jing among the Dragon Guard soldiers. Those who liked gossip said that Jing could perform the Six Jia Method, which could capture Jin generals alive and sweep away the rest. His method required seven thousand seven hundred and seventy-seven people. The imperial court deeply believed this and gave Jing an official position and tens of thousands of gold and silk. As the enemy's attacks became more urgent, Jing spoke and laughed calmly, saying: (Choosing a day to send out three hundred soldiers will bring peace.) There were also claims of Six Ding Warriors, Heavenly Pass Generals, and Big Dipper Divine Soldiers, all mostly created by Jing. Those with knowledge were worried. Jing said: (My masters will not come out unless it is extremely dangerous.) He was urged several times and changed the date again and again. Then, he opened the Xuanhua Gate and went out, ordering those guarding the city to come down and not to peep. He sat on the city tower with Zhang Shuye. The Jin soldiers divided into four wings and advanced with a roar. Jing's soldiers were defeated and retreated, falling into the Hugong River and filling it with corpses. The city gate was quickly closed. Jing hastily said to Shuye: (I must perform the method myself from below.) So, he went down the city and fled south with the crowd. That day, the Jin people ascended the city, and Emperor Qinzong went to the Jin commander's camp. It is a pity that Guo Jing fled, and the national martial arts lost its magic. Otherwise, if it had been passed down to the Boxers, they would have been able to achieve the great feat of supporting the Qing and destroying the foreign powers and would have long ago swallowed the three islands and dominated the five continents. Why would we need to wait for today's broadswords to resist Japan and national martial arts to save the country?

Carrot Hair 196

— Written by Jules Renard, Translated by Lin Qu

The Rifle (Continued)

Carrot Hair and his older brother Félix set off. They were wearing the same simple clothes they wore every day. They were somewhat disappointed because they didn’t have boots, but Lepic often told them that a real hunter looks down on boots. A real hunter's trousers are always dragging on his heels. He never rolls up his trouser legs. By walking like this in the mud and in the ploughed field, he naturally creates a pair of boots that reach up to his knees; such boots are strong, natural, and the maid at home would never dare to criticize them. (I don’t think you'll be coming back empty-handed,) said the older brother, Félix.

(I really hope I won’t,) replied Carrot Hair.

He felt awkward, and hated having the rifle butt resting on his shoulder.

(Hey!) said the older brother, Félix, (I'll let you carry the rifle all you want!)

(You're my brother,) said Carrot Hair.

When a flock of sparrows flew over, he stopped and gestured to his older brother, Félix, to stay still. The flock of sparrows flew from one fence to another. The two hunters, thinking that the sparrows were all asleep, bent over and approached silently. The sparrows didn't stay put, chirping and chattering as they flew away to another place. The two hunters stood up again, Félix frowning. Carrot Hair, although his heart was pounding, seemed to have more patience. He was afraid of the moment that would prove his cleverness.

What if he couldn't hit anything! Every delay made him feel relieved.

But this time, the sparrows seemed to be waiting for them.

(Don't shoot, you're standing too far away,) said the older brother, Félix.

(Do you think it's too far?) said Carrot Hair.

(Of course! Aiming like that will miss. We think we're aiming right, but it's actually very far off.)

So the older brother, Félix, stepped forward to prove his point. The sparrows, startled, flew away again.

But one remained, standing on a broken, swinging branch. It was wagging its tail and exposing its belly.

(I can really hit this sparrow, no mistake,) said Carrot Hair.

(Stand aside and let me see. Right, really, you've chosen well. Hurry up, lend me the rifle.)

So Carrot Hair was disarmed, his hands empty, yawning. The older brother, Félix, stood in front, replacing him, raising the rifle, aiming, and firing. The sparrow fell.

It was almost like a trick. Just now Carrot Hair had the rifle pressed against his chest. Suddenly, he had lost his rifle, but now it was back in his hands because his older brother, Félix, had returned the rifle to him, and then, playing the dog, had gone to pick up the sparrow and said: (You're still hesitating, hurry up.)

(Hurrying up might not be enough.)

(Okay, are you angry!)

(Do you want me to be happy?)

(But we hit the sparrow, so what are you arguing about? Think about it, we might not have been able to hit it at all.)

(Ah! If it were me::::)

(You or me, it's the same. I hit it today, you can hit it tomorrow.)

(Ah! Tomorrow.)

(I promise you.)

(Do I know? Last night, you promised me too.)

(I swear to you, are you satisfied?)

(Forget it!:: But if we find another sparrow right away; I can try this rifle.)

(No, it's too late now. Let's go back and let Mom fry the sparrow. I'll give you this sparrow. Stuff it in your pocket, you fool, let its beak stick out.)

The two hunters turned and went home. Sometimes they met a farmer who greeted them:

(Little rascals, at least you didn't kill that old sparrow, did you?)

Carrot Hair, flattered, forgot all his grievances. They ran home happily and triumphantly, without any resentment. Lepic, seeing them, exclaimed:

(What, Carrot Hair, you're still carrying the rifle! Have you been carrying it the whole time?)

(Almost the whole time,) Carrot Hair replied.

Economic Special Issue, Issue 20, published every Monday.

May First and the Chinese Labor Day by Luo Fu 197

(1) The Nature of May First

Eight hours of work, eight hours of education, eight hours of rest – the famous 3-8 system demand can be said to be the first manifestation of the power of laborers throughout the world after the emergence of the factory system.

Before the Industrial Revolution in the 18th century, human production activities were mainly agricultural, supplemented by family handicrafts connected to agriculture. The production of family handicrafts was isolated, without interaction. The purpose of production was mostly self-sufficiency. Therefore, production activities were highly localized. Handicraft workers could not gather together. With differing interests, there would naturally be no common demands, that is, there would be no labor movement like the modern one.

After the Industrial Revolution, advanced production techniques laid the foundation for the factory system. First, the commodities produced by factories attacked the original family handicrafts, causing their decline. Second, the emerging factories needed laborers. Thus, the relatively surplus population displaced from rural family handicrafts concentrated in the factory districts of cities, largely becoming laborers in the emerging industries. They came from rural areas with different environments and gathered in one factory, doing the same work and receiving the same treatment in the same air. Gradually, the same circumstances completely eliminated their original differences, and their character and consciousness gradually became consistent. Thus, when common interests arose, they would inevitably unite and take the same attitude, which was different from the period of family handicrafts. Those who could not unite before now had the possibility of labor movements.

At the beginning of the factory system, entrepreneurs, in order to expand their production scope as much as possible, naturally hoped that their invested capital would turn over faster and faster. The faster the capital turnover, the greater the profit, and the faster the reproduction, the greater the production scope could be expanded. Therefore, entrepreneurs tried every means to save costs as much as possible and increase output. Moreover, because the development of industry at that time was not as fast as the decline of the original family handicrafts, many declining family handicraft workers were rejected outside the factory gates. This gave entrepreneurs great convenience. They could arbitrarily choose their workers, use the lowest wages, and make them work the longest hours to increase their profits and expand their production scope.

Therefore, at the beginning of the emergence of capitalism, the improvement of production techniques instead led to the miserable fate of laborers. But at the same time, it also gave them an opportunity to unite, giving them the same intentions and the same demands. The historically famous May First labor movement was formed under such circumstances.

The May First labor movement can be said to be the initial result of the capitalist production method and the preliminary demand of world laborers. European and American customs and scholars divide labor issues into many branches, and most laborers often have the misconception that various issues can be resolved individually. In fact, the labor problem is the entire problem of the capitalist production method, and it is different from the conflict between masters and apprentices in the era of family handicrafts or guilds. Its solution must start from the whole. Working hours are not the labor problem, nor are they a part of the labor problem, but only one link in the whole labor problem. Because in what is produced by capitalism, workers do not produce for themselves, but only for wages, just as entrepreneurs produce for profit. In order to obtain greater profits, entrepreneurs must increase production. To increase production, one method is to extend working hours. This can avoid increasing costs and obtain greater profits. Therefore, the issue of working hours cannot be separated from the entire labor problem and demanded to be resolved separately.

(2) Research on the Eight-Hour Work System

The only demand of the May First labor movement was an eight-hour workday. The eight-hour workday, in a strict scientific sense, is not reasonable. According to the field research of Japanese doctor Ishihara Takatoshi, the results proved that an eight-hour workday is not an ideal and appropriate system. Dr. Ishihara studied the impact of working hours on the physiological health of female workers in different environments and climates. He found that even in the temperate East Asian countries, generally speaking, an eight-hour workday still has considerable damage to the health of workers (see the article "The Relationship between Working Hours and Climate" in the former Jiangwan Labor University Monthly). Now, many people already know that even if the health of workers is disregarded, working hours that are too long cannot increase productivity. Sometimes, they even reduce work efficiency. This situation has been adequately proven in places such as the Ford factory in the United States. Recently, the radical progress of Soviet industrial development has further confirmed this.

Before the revolution, the average daily working hours for workers in various parts of Russia were ten hours. In some places, it even exceeded fourteen to sixteen hours, just like in China. After the revolution, the Soviet government tried to shorten working hours as much as possible. The situation of gradual reduction of working hours from 1918 to 1926 is as follows:

1918: 8.5 hours per day

1922: 7.9 hours

1923: 7.8 hours

1924: 7.8 hours

1925: 7.6 hours

1926: 7.5 hours

According to reports, in 1927, the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union promulgated a decree for a seven-hour workday, which was eventually shortened to six hours per day. In the recent five years, many important industries have fully implemented the seven-hour workday. In 29 types of heavy industry and 12 types of light industry, the implementation rate has reached 82% to 92%, 90% in the timber industry, and 70% in the transportation industry. However, since the Soviet Union reduced working hours, labor productivity has increased rather than decreased. In many jobs where the seven-hour system is implemented, the average monthly productivity has increased by 8.2%, and the average daily and hourly productivity has increased by 2% to 11%. In the petroleum industry, the monthly labor productivity of each worker has increased by 13.7%, while production costs have decreased, wages have increased, and incidents of worker injury have also decreased.

However, in principle, working hours that are too long may not increase production efficiency. But if you want to shorten working hours and increase productivity at the same time, you must have excellent (production technology (as a prerequisite. Without good technology and a spirit of service ethics, it is impossible. The production relations in Soviet Russia are different, and they cannot be compared to workers who only work for wages psychologically. However, other places that implement a short-hour system can only be found in places with excellent production technology like the Ford factory in the United States, and this is for this reason.

Under today's production methods, entrepreneurs only operate for profit, and shortening working hours is a great contradiction. In order to compete with others for sales and increase personal profits, entrepreneurs naturally want the lower the production cost, the better, that is, the lower the wages, the better, and the longer the working hours, the better. Fortunately, there is an industrial reserve army, with many unemployed people. When workers reduce their work efficiency due to health damage, they can be replaced, and more laborers can be recruited. If overproduction is pressing and working hours have to be reduced, then wages can also be reduced according to the reduced time. Therefore, entrepreneurs are unwilling to have a legally mandated short-hour system. At successive Geneva World Labor Conferences, working hours have often been the subject of debate. No matter how entrepreneurs or their representatives say that working hours have been shortened, and no matter how many times there have been proposals, this issue has always remained an open question.

Therefore, the issue of working hours can only be resolved in the entire labor problem. The ultimate goal of the labor movement is the social liberation of laborers, not the resolution of partial problems. At that time, because the factory system had not been around for long, everyone did not see the drawbacks of capitalist production, but only felt that working hours were too long, so the demand for the May First Movement's 3-8 system was formed. Now that times have changed, our understanding of May First cannot be limited to the issue of working hours.

(3) The Demands of Chinese Laborers for May First

The occurrence of the Industrial Revolution and the rise of emerging industries are not consistent in various countries. The most significant difference is between advanced capitalist countries and colonies or semi-colonies. The industry of advanced capitalist countries is spontaneous, while (secondary colonies) countries such as China are not without the emergence of new industries like non-capitalist countries. However, it is not spontaneous but (externally imposed), that is, the occurrence of Chinese industry is caused by the import of industrial products from various countries (especially the import of machinery in the era of heavy industry), and its development is carried out under the aggression and control of industrial products from various countries. This dominates China's economic relations and determines the characteristics of China's labor problem.

Before the Opium War, China's economy was still in the period of rural family handicrafts. Agriculture was the main method of production, and family handicrafts could be relatively self-sufficient. However, after the surplus commodities of various countries invaded the Chinese countryside, because of their low prices and good quality, they were like mercury seeping into the ground, penetrating everywhere. The original Chinese family handicraft products naturally declined completely like fallen leaves swept away by the autumn wind when competing with them. The Chinese small farmers who could have been self-sufficient had to rely on the supply of imported commodities from various countries. Agriculture also declined due to a lack of capital. Thus, Chinese farmers had no choice but to escape from the countryside, like the farmers in England after the Industrial Revolution in the early 18th century, and sell their labor in the cities to maintain their survival.

However, when Chinese farmers fled to the cities and transformed into industrial laborers, their experiences were clearly different from those of farmers in England in the early 18th century in two aspects. First, at the beginning of the factory system in capitalist countries, although the population that emerging industries could accommodate was far below the population squeezed out of agriculture and family handicrafts, there were still many new markets that had not been opened up at that time, and colonial policies could also alleviate this relatively surplus population to a considerable extent. In China, agriculture and family handicrafts declined even more rapidly, while the development of industry no longer had the superior conditions of advanced capitalist countries. Moreover, due to the pressure of economic aggression from various countries, the development of national industry was extremely difficult. The farmers who fled from the countryside found it even more difficult to find employment.

This reason determines the complexity of the types and levels of Chinese laborers. The distribution of the Chinese population is not like that of capitalist countries, which is mainly differentiated into the most numerous industrial workers and a few capitalists. Instead, in addition to a small part who can enter factories and become industrial workers, most of the population either becomes unemployed, day laborers with no fixed jobs, bandits who take risks, and the basis of the army that is brave in internal wars but unable to resist external aggression, or they reduce their living standards to an unspeakable level and still remain in the countryside, waiting for the arrival of death.

Second, the core of the labor problem in advanced capitalist countries is the confrontation between workers and capitalists. In China, national capitalism cannot be fully developed, and there will not be large capitalists like Krupp, Rockefeller, Mitsui, and Mitsubishi who monopolize the national economy. Moreover, the tragic fate of various Chinese laborers is not only promoted by the aggression of capitalist countries, but also by the convenience of various countries to exploit Chinese raw materials and cheap labor. They have set up factories in China one after another. Generally speaking, most of the labor-capital relations in China are not the relationship between domestic laborers and domestic capitalists, but the relationship with foreign capitalists. In the heavy industry sector, 80% of all mining and manufacturing is in the hands of foreigners. Light industries such as textile mills and flour mills are also operated by foreigners. If there is a labor-capital conflict in China, then this conflict is bound to occur more often between Chinese workers and foreign capitalists. This is the characteristic of China's labor problem, that is, even for industrial laborers, the core of the problem is different from what occurs in capitalist countries. Therefore, the crux of China's labor problem lies in resisting economic aggression. This is true not only for Chinese industrial workers, but also for Chinese entrepreneurs in their infancy. The failure of their industries is due to the dumping of surplus commodities and the squeezing of economic power by capitalist countries. In this regard, their enthusiasm for resisting imperialism is the same as that of industrial workers.

Because Chinese laborers are of different types, their understanding and demands for May First are naturally different. However, there is one point on which they are common, as mentioned above, that is, resisting imperialist aggression. They know that all the tragic fates are caused by imperialist aggression. If there is no way to solve it, then there is no way to do anything. Therefore, the demand of Chinese laborers for May First is not only to demand their own liberation, but also to use their greatest strength to unite with the entire nation to seek liberation, resist foreign economic aggression, and seek industrial independence and self-sufficiency. Standing on the same front and not competing with each other and giving others an opportunity to take advantage of them, then China's industry will not be able to extricate itself, and the liberation of laborers will probably only become a mirage.

The Peasant in the Rural Economic Bankruptcy by He Bing 198

(1) The Process of Rural Economic Bankruptcy in China. Radek once pointed out that the increase in taxes and the invasion of commodities were the main reasons for the rural economic bankruptcy in China. The invasion of commodities is indeed a manifestation of imperialist aggression, and the increase in taxes is also indirectly promoted by imperialism. Directly and indirectly, the bankruptcy of the Chinese countryside is all affected by imperialism. Since the Opium War, China's indemnities and foreign debts have increased day by day. The final burden must be transferred to the peasants in the form of increased taxes. In order to compete for the Chinese market, the capitalist countries have all protected the warlords and used them as pawns. Conflicts of interest have increased civil wars. Therefore, according to investigations, China's taxes increased by 39.3% from the founding of the Republic to the 17th year of the Republic of China, and the continuous import of surplus commodities promoted the decline of rural handicrafts, making the lives of peasants lose their relative independence. Also, for the plunder of raw materials, the original crops have been changed. For example, in Shaanxi, which is known as ("the best land"), there is recently a saying ("cotton enters the pass, wheat goes up the mountain"). In the northeastern provinces, the acreage of tobacco cultivation is increasing day by day, and the peasants' self-sufficient plants such as rice and wheat are gradually being excluded. The prevalence of this kind of raw material planting makes it inevitable for Chinese small farmers to rely on the market, that is, their fate of survival is remotely manipulated by foreign big capitalists. For example, during the world economic panic in 1929, the number of northeastern small farmers who died among rotten soybeans was increasing every day.

(2) The Daily Life of Chinese Small Farmers. There are many levels of so-called peasants, from landlords who live on land rent to hired farmers who have no land to stand on. Their lives cannot be compared on the same day. Even for the common so-called self-cultivating farmers, semi-self-cultivating farmers, and tenant farmers, the levels are extremely complex. For example, the Academia Sinica's survey of Wuxi villages found no less than forty kinds of land ownership forms. The lives of farmers with different land ownership must be very different (the beginning of the study of Chinese agricultural economic research). However, in this group of peasants with complex levels, we still cannot find where their center of gravity lies. For example, according to the survey of the Land Committee of the Kuomintang Central Committee in the 16th year of the Republic of China, the number of Chinese farmers who cultivated and accumulated one to ten mu of land accounted for 44% of the population, but only occupied 6% of the land. Regardless of whether this number is credible, it is an undeniable fact that Chinese small farmers are dominant. As in the 1928 edition of the China Yearbook published by the Toa Dobunko, the distribution of land in China of 10 mu or less accounted for 42.3% of the total area, which is sufficient to prove the prevalence of Chinese small farmers. Moreover, this kind of small land is not concentrated in one place. There are often farm families with less than 10 mu, and their land is scattered in various places, sometimes as many as five or six pieces, each piece usually two or three li away (see the Outline of Rural Sociology).

Small farmers are poor farmers. The fragmentation and smallness of their cultivated land area have a history. Common people think that China's system of partitioning property is the culprit, but the main reason is the poverty of the peasants. According to various investigations, such as Wuhu, Yanshan, Chengdu, the suburbs of Beiping, and the four suburbs of Shanghai, where it is easier to engage in sideline businesses, most of the farmers are in debt. Some people use an income of 150 yuan per year as the lifeline of the farmers, but generally speaking, the income of each small farm family in various places rarely exceeds 150 yuan per year. In the past, remittances from farmers living abroad were barely enough to help in emergencies, but recently this source has been cut off, and the income from family handicrafts has long been eliminated. What the farmers have is only borrowing.

However, not all farmers are qualified to borrow. Whether it is private borrowing, pawning, or borrowing from cooperatives (only available in a few places), they must have collateral. The main collateral of farmers is land. But in this time of frequent natural disasters and man-made calamities, the farmers' loans are increasing day by day. For example, the Jiangsu Farmers Bank's loans are used by farmers less for production and more for repaying high-interest loans and buying food. Therefore, farmers' land is being confiscated because they are unable to repay their debts everywhere. According to Mr. Qiao Zuoming's survey of Kunshan, Nantong, and Suxian, the reduction of cultivated land area of farmers, taking 1905 as a base of 100%, had been reduced to 41% by 1924 (Kunshan has cultivated land), not to mention the disaster-stricken areas in various places. Land is the main means of production for farmers. It is also where life depends. If this is not guaranteed, the situation of daily life can be imagined. In terms of food, farmers in various places sell valuable agricultural products and keep the cheap ones for their own use (see the Rural Survey Report of Wuchang County). Even the diet varies with the season. Farmers in North China eat coarse grains in winter, and they do not consider other things. Farmers in various counties in Shaanxi and Shanxi often sell ("the food of the previous night") to pay taxes and rent. Their plight is indescribable.

Opium, red pills, and other drugs have recently become popular in rural areas in various provinces. The initiators are local military police ruffians, who monopolize the planting and profit from it, but the poverty of the farmers in various places is also the reason. In the places that the author has experienced, there are quite a few farmers who swallow opium and red pills. This is because the diet is not refined, the nutrition is insufficient, and the health is declining day by day. If they don't do this, they can't work. How can the farmers be willing to degenerate? If the diet is like this, other things can be known. According to various surveys, even in the so-called wealthy rural areas, such as the suburbs of Shanghai and Beiping, there are often more than 50% of farm families who have no clothing expenses every year, and other expenses are even less.

(3) The Phenomenon of the Deterioration of Peasant Life. The commonness and breadth of disasters in China can be said to be unparalleled in the world. For example, the drought in the Northwest in 1929, the flood in Central China in 1920, and the ("rich disaster") in the Southeast in 1932 (that is, a bumper harvest becomes a disaster, and counties in Jiangnan and Jiangbei all call it a rich disaster) all resulted in the loss of tens of millions of people and the submergence of countless agricultural products. It is also to be expected that people and animals eat each other and there is nothing left of grass and trees in the disaster area. Although disasters seem to be natural, they are actually man-made. Forests are felled, and water conservancy is not repaired for many years. These are the main reasons for the disasters, and the increasing poverty of small farmers and the exhaustion of agricultural production capital are also the causes of disasters. Analyzing the areas with the most disasters in recent decades, that is, the places where imperialist aggression is the most severe and the degree of impoverishment of peasants is the deepest (see the New Creation Agricultural Special Issue), it is not difficult to see the truth. Popularists advocate improving production as a means of improving rural areas, but the facts show that if the social system is not good, a bumper harvest can also become a disaster, so there is no need to improve production.

The lives of farmers in disaster areas are not worth discussing, and even in non-disaster areas, most rural areas are similar to disaster areas. In western Zhejiang, due to the decline of silkworm farming, there was also a human market last year. Husbands carry their wives, and fathers bring their daughters, wandering around and shouting, selling them by the catty, which is no different from the situation in the Northwest during the severe drought.

During the Yangzhou land tax turmoil, farmers destroyed the county town. The rice looting in Wuxi and the (eating the rich turmoil) of old women also caused disturbances for a long time. When the author went to Shengze, Wujiang last year, which has been known as (the hometown of ten thousand silks at sunrise) for hundreds of years, there was news of family suicides almost every day. Recently, the adoption of improved silkworm seeds in Zhejiang has also aroused peasant riots. Last year, farmers were unable to afford the one yuan for buying silkworm seeds, so they endured the spring and grew old in vain. Now the improved seeds are twice the price of the native seeds, and the full adoption is beyond the ability of the farmers. Regardless of whether there is any inside story, is it not reckless to think that this is improving the rural areas? Recently, there are quite a few people talking about (returning to the countryside), but the facts show that the claims of (idealists) are not difficult to prove to be a fantasy.

(4) Rural Bankruptcy and Labor Issues. China's peasant problem and labor problem are closely related and cannot be separated. It can also be said that today, it is better for us to pay more attention to the peasant problem than to the labor problem, because the bankruptcy of the rural economy is the key to the labor problem.

Due to the invasion of imperialist commodities, the extortion of exorbitant taxes and levies, and the frequent occurrence of man-made and natural disasters, peasants are uneasy in their occupations and have no way to live without fleeing. According to surveys in various places, the peasants, who were known to be as quiet as a dead swamp, have been moving so rapidly in recent years that they can be compared to raging waves. This is because they have no way to live without fleeing. Most of the farmers who leave the village in various places become laborers, and women become prostitutes. Otherwise, they either die in ditches or flow into the path of bandits and soldiers, which exacerbates the collapse of the rural economy.

However, the characteristic of China's economy is only that it is a colony or (secondary colony), that is, the industry is controlled by imperialists. Therefore, although the countryside is bankrupt, urban industry has not been able to develop proportionally. The emerging industries have not been able to absorb even one-tenth of the population that has crowded out of the countryside. If these people become bandits or soldiers, they can threaten the security of the city and destroy the prosperity of industry. If they are unemployed, they will increase the severity of the labor problem. The more unemployed there are, the more difficult it is for workers to find employment, the longer the working hours, and the shorter the wages must be.

From the perspective of industry, China is an industrially backward country and the tail end of commodity dumping by imperialist countries. So-called international trade is only to accommodate surplus commodities and contribute raw materials. If we want to develop China's industry, industrial products must only be sold domestically, and the only domestic market is the countryside. The peasants are so poor that they cannot buy, so if we want to prosper industry,

Long-Term Interbank Market Conditions 200

Situation at the End of the Long Term 201

Yesterday was the end of April. According to regulations, everything had to be concluded yesterday. The long-term loans from Ningbo banks amounted to no less than two million, all of which were either collected, transferred, or newly made on that day, with all amounts clearly handed over. The Stock Market Last Week, Amidst the Tug-of-War Between Bulls and Bears 203

Waves and fluctuations ultimately led to the dominance of the bulls.

Prices rose by several jiao to two yuan and two jiao and a half.

Last week, from April 24th to 29th, the bond market at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange was relatively active and sensitive. Due to the impending deadline for April futures trading, there was a squeeze between short and long positions in the market, with considerable competition. The waves and fluctuations ultimately led to the dominance of the bulls. In terms of the situation, there were also signs of easing, with Japanese troops gradually withdrawing, and Tianjin and Beijing temporarily safe. However, the battle at Nantianmen was still fierce, and people could not help but feel uneasy. On Monday, the rise and fall were quite rapid, and the short squeeze was also strong. Among them, only the morning closing saw a slight pullback due to the expiration of long positions, with the rest all rising. The multi-day increase was as high as two yuan. Tuesday was the last day for April futures, with the struggle between long and short positions being particularly intense. Market prices rose and fell rapidly, resulting in a skewed result, with some rising by more than one yuan and others falling by five or six jiao. This was because both long and short positions were urgently seeking to settle, each going their own way, making it impossible to be aligned. On Wednesday, only May futures were traded. Coincidentally, the Japanese troops in Qinhuangdao and Luandong suddenly announced their withdrawal, and people's hearts were uplifted, and market prices rose by another yuan or so. On Thursday, June futures were added for auction, but they failed to open. After several days of rising, there was a slight reaction. Guangbang (Guangdong traders) sold heavily, and prices fell by about half a yuan. On Friday, the April futures settlement was handled and the market was closed. On Saturday, trading decreased sharply, and the market was slightly stagnant, with mixed ups and downs, and the numbers were quite small. In summary, the market price for the week rose by several jiao to two yuan and two jiao and a half compared to the previous week. Observing the entire week, the environment was good, causing a short squeeze, and the bulls benefited a lot. After the settlement, the market gradually became quieter. If there are no special changes in the situation, there may be a period of stable consolidation. The total transaction volume was 49,272,000 yuan, of which spot transactions were only 17,000 yuan. Futures accounted for a total of 19,300,000, with troop reduction accounting for over 7,700,000, the 1924 Customs Bonds accounting for over 8,700,000, the 2021 Customs Bonds accounting for over 9,810,000, and the troop reorganization bonds accounting for only 2,340,000. The rest ranged from tens of thousands to over two hundred thousand. The trading volume of June futures was very small, with a total of only 130,000, with only troop reorganization bonds and 1924 Customs Bonds providing a slight boost.
